(0) And Hafiz al-Din al-Kabir is the sixth in the chain, and he is Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Nasr al-Imam Hafiz al-Din, died in 693 AH, and he was an imam, ascetic, pious, comprehensive in types of knowledge; he studied under Shams al-A'imma Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Sattar al-Kurdi, and he is the seventh in the chain, connected from the narrators of al-Tabsira, and he was described as Shams al-Din; the author of al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a says: He is the absolute teacher of the imams; he traveled to Transoxiana and studied in Samarqand under Shaykh al-Islam al-Marghinani, the author of al-Hidaya, and he excelled in knowledge of the madhhab, revival of the science of usul, and fiqh; he died in 642 AH. And al-Marghinani is the eighth in the chain, connected from the narrators of al-Tabsira, and his name is Burhan al-Din Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Abi Bakr ibn 'Abd al-Jalil al-Marghinani (1); he was an imam, jurist, comprehensive in sciences; among his works: al-Muntaqa, Nashr al-Madhhab, and al-Hidaya. And he studied under famous imams such as Najm al-Din 'Umar al-Nasafi and Diya' al-Din Muhammad ibn al-Husayn. And the last is the ninth in the chain. And his name is Diya' al-Din Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Nasir al-Yarsukhi (2), and he studied under 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi. And 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi is the student of Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, and he is Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi (3). He studied under Imam Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi; indeed he is the most reliable of the students of Abu al-Mu'in, and among his works is Mizan al-Usul fi Nata'ij al-'Uqul. And I think that the connection of the chain of narrators beginning with 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi and ending with Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam confirms for us that al-Tabsira is a book closely connected to its author Abu al-Mu'in.

Commentary
This passage presents the chain of narrators (sanad) of Tabsirat al-Adilla, tracing the transmission of the book from the author Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi down to later scholars. It begins by mentioning that the second narrator in the chain is Saraj al-Din al-Qari', then lists each narrator with brief biographical details: their full names, scholarly achievements, teachers, and dates. The chain progresses through 'Ala' al-Din al-Sayrafi, Jalal al-Din al-Karlani, 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Bukhari, Hafiz al-Din al-Kabir, Shams al-A'imma al-Kurdi, al-Marghinani, Diya' al-Din al-Yarsukhi, and finally 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi, who is a direct student of the author. The passage concludes by emphasizing that this continuous chain confirms the close connection of Tabsirat to its author.

The Chain of Transmission of Tabsirat al-Adilla
Describes the chain of narrators linking Tabsirat to Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the chain of transmission (sanad) of Tabsirat al-Adilla and how it confirms the book's direct link to its author, Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi.

Core Idea
The sanad of Tabsirat al-Adilla links directly to its author through eight reliable transmitters.

This lesson examines the chain of narrators that transmitted Tabsirat al-Adilla from its author, Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, down to later scholars. By tracing each link, we can see how the book's authenticity was preserved. The passage names key figures and shows that the chain is unbroken, confirming the work's close connection to its author.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key transmitters
Read the passage and list the names mentioned in order from al-Marghinani back to Abu al-Mu'in. Notice how each scholar studied under the next.
Al-Marghinani is the eighth, Diya' al-Din is the ninth, and so on.
2
Understand the chain's final link
Pay attention to the final statement that the chain from 'Ala' al-Din to Kamal al-Din confirms the book's connection to Abu al-Mu'in. This is the key takeaway.
3
Reflect on the purpose of sanad
Ask yourself: Why is it important to trace the chain of transmission for a book like this? The answer lies in preserving scholarly authenticity.
Sanad is a hallmark of Islamic traditional learning.

على شيخ الإسلام المرغيناني صاحب الهداية وبرع في معرفة المذهب، وإحياء علم الأصول، والفقه توفى سنة ٦٤٢هـ. والمرغيناني هو الثامن في السند متصلا من رواة التبصرة، واسمه برهان الدين أبو الحسن على بي أبي بكر بن عبد الجليل المرغيناني، كان إماما فقيها جامعا للعلوم، من تصانيفه المنتقى، ونشر المذهب، والهداية. وتفقه على مشاهير الأئمة مثل نجم الدين عمر النسفي، وضياء الدين محمد بن الحسين. والأخير هو التاسع في السند. واسمه ضياء الدين محمد بن الحسين بن ناصر اليرسوخي، وقد تفقه على علاء الدين السمرقندي. وعلاء الدين السمرقندي هو تلميذ أبي المعين النسفي، وهو أبو بكر محمد بن أحمد السمرقندي. تفقه على الإمام أبي المعين النسفي بل هو أوثق تلاميذ أبي المعين، ومن مؤلفاته ميزان الأصول في نتائج العقول. وأحسب أن اتصال سند الرواة بدءًا بعلاء الدين السمرقندي، وانتهاء بكمال الدين بن الهمام يؤكد لنا أن التبصرة كتاب وثيق الصلة بمؤلفه أبي المعين.
Upon Shaykh al-Islam al-Marghinani, author of al-Hidaya, who excelled in knowledge of the madhhab, revival of the science of usul, and fiqh, died in 642 AH. And al-Marghinani is the eighth in the chain directly from the transmitters of al-Tabsira, and his name is Burhan al-Din Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Abi Bakr ibn 'Abd al-Jalil al-Marghinani; he was an imam, a jurist, comprehensive in sciences; among his works are al-Muntaqa, Nashr al-Madhhab, and al-Hidaya. He studied under prominent imams such as Najm al-Din 'Umar al-Nasafi and Diya' al-Din Muhammad ibn al-Husayn. And the latter is the ninth in the chain. And his name is Diya' al-Din Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Nasir al-Yarsukhi, and he studied under 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi. And 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi is a student of Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, and he is Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi. He studied under Imam Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi; indeed he is the most reliable of Abu al-Mu'in's students, and among his works is Mizan al-Usul fi Nata'ij al-'Uqul. And I think that the connection of the chain of transmitters starting with 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi and ending with Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam confirms to us that al-Tabsira is a book closely linked to its author Abu al-Mu'in.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage describes the chain of transmission (sanad) of Tabsirat al-Adilla. It begins by identifying al-Marghinani, the author of al-Hidaya, as the eighth transmitter in the chain, listing his name, titles, and works. Then it traces further: al-Marghinani studied under Najm al-Din 'Umar al-Nasafi and Diya' al-Din Muhammad ibn al-Husayn, who is the ninth transmitter. Diya' al-Din studied under 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi. 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi is a student of Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi himself, and he is described as the most reliable student. The passage concludes that this continuous chain from 'Ala' al-Din to Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam confirms that the book Tabsirat al-Adilla is authentically linked to its author, Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi. The passage thus establishes the scholarly credibility and direct textual transmission of the work.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the chain only lists names without significance.
Correction: The chain actually proves the book's authenticity by showing an unbroken line of reliable transmitters.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The chain of transmission demonstrates that Tabsirat al-Adilla is authentically connected to its author through a series of reliable scholars.

The Virtues of Umar ibn al-Khattab
Al-Nasafi enumerates three virtues of Umar establishing his second rank.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key virtues that establish Umar's preeminent rank after Abu Bakr according to al-Nasafi.

Core Idea
Umar's title al-Faruq and the Companions' consensus confirm his second rank.

Al-Nasafi now turns to the virtues of Umar, systematically listing the reasons for his elevated status. This passage not only highlights Umar's individual merits but also demonstrates the communal recognition of his excellence, providing a clear doctrinal foundation for the Sunni belief in the caliphal hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the phrase 'فبه أظهر الله دينه' and the reference to 'الفاروق'.
2
Identify the three virtues
The passage lists three distinct reasons for Umar's rank. Find each one: (1) his role in manifesting religion and distinguishing truth, (2) Abu Bakr's statement and the lack of objection, (3) the conquests and guidance of people.
These are not just historical facts but theological arguments for Umar's status.
3
Understand the significance of consensus
Note that the Companions' silence when Abu Bakr praised Umar is taken as tacit approval, establishing a consensus (ijma) on Umar's merit.
Ijmāʿ is a key source of knowledge in Sunni theology.
4
Reflect on al-Faruq
The title al-Faruq ('the distinguisher') is directly linked to Umar's role in separating truth from falsehood. This is not just a nickname but a doctrinal indicator of his divinely inspired judgment.
Common misunderstanding: al-Faruq is sometimes seen as a mere epithet, but it carries deep theological weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يتحدث عن فضل عمر، فيعدد الأمور التي تضع عمر في المرتبة الثانية بعد أبي بكر، فبه أظهر الله دينه وبه فرق بين الحق والباطل، ولهذا سمي الفاروق، ثم إن الصحابة سمعوا أبا بكر وهو يقول: "لو سألني الله تعالى يوم القيامة من وليت عليهم؟ لقلت: خير أهلك" ولم ينكر أحد ذلك، وببركة إمامته افتتحت بلاد العجم، وهدى الله ما لا يحصى من الناس.
Then he discusses the virtue of Umar, enumerating the matters that place Umar in the second rank after Abu Bakr: through him Allah manifested His religion and through him He distinguished between truth and falsehood, and for this he was called al-Faruq. Then indeed the Companions heard Abu Bakr saying: 'If Allah the Exalted asked me on the Day of Resurrection whom I appointed over them, I would say: the best of your people.' And no one denied that. And by the blessing of his leadership, the lands of the non-Arabs were conquered, and Allah guided countless people.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage describes the virtues of Umar ibn al-Khattab as enumerated by al-Nasafi. It states that Umar occupies the second rank after Abu Bakr. The reasons given include that through Umar Allah manifested Islam and distinguished truth from falsehood, earning him the title al-Faruq. Additionally, Abu Bakr himself is reported to have said that if Allah asked him whom he appointed, he would say the best of the people, referring to Umar, and no Companion objected. Finally, the conquests of non-Arab lands occurred during Umar's caliphate, and many people were guided. This establishes Umar's high status and the consensus of the Companions on his merit.

Correction: Al-Nasafi explains that Umar was called al-Faruq because through him Allah distinguished between truth and falsehood, making the title a reflection of his divinely guided role in separating right from wrong.

Are you using that influence to guide others to truth, or are you more concerned with your own comfort? What will you change today to be a means of guidance for even one person?

Uthman's Rank and Merits in Sunni Dogma
Al-Nasafi defines Uthman's rank and lists his proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on Uthman ibn Affan's rank as the third caliph, the merits that support it, and the refutation of those who place Ali before him.

Core Idea
Uthman's rank after Abu Bakr and Umar is proven by his sacrifices and prophetic honors.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi addresses a sensitive question about the ranking of the early caliphs. He affirms the Sunni consensus that Uthman ibn Affan holds the third position after Abu Bakr and Umar, countering the views of two hadith scholars who argued for Ali's precedence. Let us examine the evidence he presents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the English translation. Let the author's words settle.
Notice the direct refutation of named individuals.
2
Identify the opposing scholars
Find the two hadith scholars who preferred Ali over Uthman. Understand that this is an internal debate within hadith circles.
Al-Husayn ibn al-Fadl al-Bajali and Muhammad ibn Ishaq ibn Khuzayma.
3
List the three merits of Uthman
The passage enumerates three distinct merits: financial sacrifice, the hand-in-hand pledge, and the angels' shyness. Write them down.
Each merit is a direct proof of Uthman's high station.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: How does each merit support Uthman's rank? Why are these particular honors important in Sunni theology?
They show divine approval through the Prophet's actions and revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتحدث عن فضل عثمان، مبينا أنه يأتي في المرتبة بعد أبي بكر وعمر، خلافا لقول الحسين بن الفضل البجلي، ومحمد بن إسحاق بن خزيمة من أهل الحديث فإنهما يقدمان عليا على عثمان. ويعدد مناقب عثمان: ومنها - الأموال الكثيرة التي صرفها في نصرة الدين، وإقامة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إحدى يديه مقام يد عثمان في بيعة الرضوان، والإخبار بأن الملائكة تستحي منه.
And he discusses the virtue of Uthman, showing that he comes in rank after Abu Bakr and Umar, contrary to the statement of al-Husayn ibn al-Fadl al-Bajali and Muhammad ibn Ishaq ibn Khuzayma from the people of hadith, for they give precedence to Ali over Uthman. And he enumerates the merits of Uthman, among which are: the abundant wealth he spent in supporting the religion, and the Prophet's placing one of his hands in place of Uthman's hand in the Pledge of al-Ridwan, and the report that the angels are shy of him.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage presents al-Nasafi's discussion of Uthman's virtue. He states that Uthman is third in rank after Abu Bakr and Umar, refuting the view of al-Husayn ibn al-Fadl al-Bajali and Muhammad ibn Ishaq ibn Khuzayma, two hadith scholars who considered Ali ahead of Uthman. Then al-Nasafi lists several merits of Uthman: his great financial sacrifices for Islam, the honor of the Prophet using Uthman's hand in the pledge of Ridwan (since Uthman was absent), and the prophetic report that the angels feel shy before Uthman. These points establish Uthman's high status and answer those who contest his rank.

Key Terms

مناقب عثمان
الملائكة تستحي منه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some hadith scholars, like al-Bajali and Ibn Khuzayma, considered Ali superior to Uthman in rank.
Correction: The Sunni consensus, affirmed by al-Nasafi, holds that Uthman is third after Abu Bakr and Umar, supported by explicit merits from the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Uthman ibn Affan occupies the third rank among the Rightly Guided Caliphs, supported by his unparalleled charity and prophetic honors.

Virtue of Ali and Conclusion of 'Tabsirat al-Adilla'
Al-Nasafi ends his discussion on the imamate with Ali's virtue and completes the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the emphasis Al-Nasafi places on Ali's virtues as a model leader and how he concludes his major work.

Core Idea
Ali's excellence in knowledge, piety, ijtihad, and bravery marks the ideal imam.

In this final passage of his book, Al-Nasafi highlights the qualities that made Ali ibn Abi Talib the best of his time during his caliphate. He then brings his great work to a close with thanks to Allah. This lesson explores the significance of this conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: first the virtue of Ali, then the conclusion of the book.
The passage is short but packed with meaning.
2
Identify the four qualities
The passage lists four specific qualities of Ali: knowledge, piety, ijtihad, and bravery. Note each one and consider why they are highlighted.
These qualities define the ideal leader in Al-Nasafi's view.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Think about why Al-Nasafi ends his book with Ali's virtue and then thanks Allah. What does this tell us about the author's intent?
The conclusion ties together the themes of leadership and divine assistance.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage concludes al-Nasafi's discussion on the imamate by praising Ali ibn Abi Talib. It states that Ali was the best of his era during his caliphate because of his knowledge, piety (wara'), independent reasoning (ijtihad), and bravery. No specific refutation is given here; it simply affirms his merit. Then the commentator (or author) signals the end of the book 'Tabsirat al-Adilla', thanking Allah for assistance and success. This serves as a conclusion to the entire work.

Defending Abu Hanifa from Tashbīh: The Reports of Mā'iyyah
Al-Nasafi refutes tashbīh and ta'tīl by analyzing reports of mā'iyyah from Abu Hanifa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi defends Abu Hanifa from accusations of anthropomorphism by analyzing the reports of mā'iyyah and showing the balanced Maturidi position on attributes.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa's alleged 'mā'iyyah' is not anthropomorphism but a reference to God's hidden name.

In this passage, al-Nasafi addresses a controversial attribution: that Abu Hanifa taught a 'what-ness' (mā'iyyah) for God. He carefully examines the sources of this report, suggests an orthodox interpretation, and then cites Hammad ibn Abi Hanifa's rejection of both anthropomorphism and complete negation. This lesson unpacks how al-Nasafi defends the Hanafi-Maturidi tradition from the extremes of tashbīh and ta'tīl.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic carefully, then the translation. Note the names mentioned and the argument flow.
Pay attention to how al-Nasafi structures his defense.
2
Identify the key claims
The passage makes several claims: (a) reports of mā'iyyah are not textually explicit, (b) the interpretation comes from Dirar, (c) Abū Hanīfa might have meant the hidden name, (d) Hammad's statement shows a balanced position, (e) the attribution ultimately comes from Ghassan.
3
Analyze the proof from the prophetic supplication
How does al-Nasafi use the hadith to support his interpretation? Notice the structure of the argument.
The hadith is cited as evidence for the hidden name concept.
4
Understand the position of Hammad ibn Abi Hanifa
Hammad rejects both tashbīh (Muqatil) and ta'tīl (Jahm). Why is this significant for the Maturidi school?
5
Reflect on the overall argument
The passage ends with the note that the attribution to Abu Hanifa is weak. How does this strengthen the Maturidi rejection of anthropomorphism?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول: إن من روى عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله القول بالمائية لم يرو عنه التفسير نصا. وذكر أبو محمد النوبختي نصا أن تفسيره لم يرد إلا عن ضرار، وقد بينا أنها محتملة ومن الجائز أنه أراد ذلك الاسم أي الله تعالى اسم لا يعلمه إلا هو، ولو كان مراده هذا فهو موافق لما ورد به الخبر، وهو الدعاء المأثور عن النبي عليه السلام فيمن أصابه هم (اللهم أنا عبدك وابن عبدك وابن أمتك ناصيتي بيدك ماض في حكمك عدل في قضاؤك، أسألك بكل اسم هو لك سميت به نفسك أو أنزلته في كتابك أو علمته أحداً من خلقك أو استأثرت به في علم الغيب عندك أن تجعل القرآن ربيع قلبي ونور صدري وجلاء حزني وذهاب همي). وإذا كان هذا محتملا لا معنى لصرف ذلك إلى إثبات المجانسة والمماثلة مع ظهوره في التبرئ عن التشبيه، وثبتت الرواية عن حماد بن أبي حنيفة، وكان متكلما عالما بمذاهب أبيه أنه قال: لا نفر عن الصفة فرار جهم، ولا نصفه صفة مقاتل بن سليمان، وإنما قال ذلك لأن مقاتلا كان مشبها، وجهم كان معطلا، فتبرأ منهما على أن هذا كله تكلف لأن القول بالمائية غير ثابت عنه على ما مر، وإنما أخذ المتكلمون نسبة القول بالمائية إليه عن غسان فإنه قال: كان أبو حنيفة وأصحابه
Then we say: Whoever reports from Abu Hanifa, may God have mercy on him, the statement about mā'iyyah, did not report from him the interpretation textually. And Abu Muhammad al-Nawbakhti mentioned textually that his interpretation was only transmitted from Dirar. And we have explained that it is ambiguous, and it is possible that he intended that name, i.e., the name of God Almighty which none knows but He. And if his intention was this, then it agrees with what has come in the report, which is the supplication transmitted from the Prophet, peace be upon him, for one afflicted with grief: 'O God, I am Your servant, son of Your servant, son of Your maidservant; my forelock is in Your hand, Your decree is accomplished in me, Your judgment in me is just. I ask You by every name that is Yours, by which You have named Yourself, or revealed in Your Book, or taught anyone of Your creation, or kept with Yourself in the knowledge of the unseen with You, to make the Qur'an the spring of my heart, the light of my chest, the remover of my sadness, and the dispeller of my grief.' And if this is possible, there is no meaning to turning that to affirming homogeneity and likeness, while it is apparent in disavowal of tashbīh. And the report is established from Hammad ibn Abi Hanifa, who was a mutakallim and knowledgeable in his father's doctrines, that he said: 'We do not flee from attributes as Jahm fled, nor do we describe Him with the description of Muqatil ibn Sulayman.' And he only said that because Muqatil was a mushabbih (anthropomorphist) and Jahm was a mu‘attil (denier of attributes), so he disavowed them both. But all of this is forced because the statement about mā'iyyah is not established from him according to what has passed. Rather, the mutakallimūn only took the attribution of the statement about mā'iyyah to him from Ghassan, for he said: 'Abu Hanifa and his companions...'
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage addresses reports attributing the doctrine of mā'iyyah (what-ness) to Abu Hanifa. The author argues that those who report this do not provide an explicit interpretive text from him. Al-Nawbakhti is cited as stating that the only interpretation of mā'iyyah from Abu Hanifa comes via Dirar. The author suggests that Abu Hanifa might have meant the hidden name of God, as supported by a prophetic supplication. Thus, interpreting it as implying anthropomorphism is unfounded. The author then cites Hammad ibn Abi Hanifa, who rejected both the extreme anthropomorphism of Muqatil ibn Sulayman and the extreme negation (ta‘tīl) of Jahm ibn Safwan. Hammad's statement shows a balanced Maturidi position. Finally, the author notes that the attribution of mā'iyyah to Abu Hanifa likely originates from Ghassan al-Murji'i, and even then it is not certain. The passage concludes abruptly but clearly defends Abu Hanifa from being associated with tashbīh.

Key Terms
المائية (al-mā'iyyah)
التشبيه (al-tashbīh)
التعطيل (al-ta‘tīl)
ضرار (Dirar)
حماد بن أبي حنيفة (Hammad ibn Abi Hanifa)
غسان (Ghassan)
المتشبه (al-mushabbih)
المعطل (al-mu‘attil)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abu Hanifa believed in a literal mā'iyyah for God implying He has a 'what-ness' like creatures.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows this report is unreliable and can be interpreted as God's hidden name, and Abu Hanifa's son Hammad explicitly rejected anthropomorphism.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, from whom does the interpretation of mā'iyyah attributed to Abu Hanifa primarily come?
A) Hammad ibn Abi Hanifa
B) Dirar
C) Ghassan al-Murji'i
D) Abu Muhammad al-Nawbakhti

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi defends Abu Hanifa from anthropomorphism by showing that reports of mā'iyyah are weak and can be interpreted as God's hidden name, while Hammad ibn Abi Hanifa's statement shows the Maturidi rejection of both tashbīh and ta'tīl.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of Allah's attributes, do you ever find yourself inadvertently picturing something limited or human-like? How does this passage's insistence on transcendence force you to re-examine your own mental images of God, and what concrete step can you take today to purify your tawhid?
?
The supplication in the lesson includes the words 'or kept with Yourself in the knowledge of the unseen with You.' How often do you remember that Allah's names and essence are far beyond what you know? How can this awareness transform your humility and your sincerity in du'a starting now?
?
Hammad ibn Abi Hanifa said, 'We do not flee from attributes as Jahm fled, nor do we describe Him with the description of Muqatil.' Which extreme are you personally more prone to—neglecting God's attributes due to fear of anthropomorphism, or casual, imaginative descriptions of God? What one change in your daily remembrance can you make to stay on the balanced path?

The Chain of Transmission from Abu Hanifa to Samarqand
Nasafi enumerates the early scholars of Abu Hanifa's school in Transoxiana and Khurasan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi establishes an unbroken chain of scholars transmitting Abu Hanifa's creed in Transoxiana, particularly in Samarqand.

Core Idea
The Maturidi school traces its creed directly to Abu Hanifa through a known chain.

This passage from Nasafi's Tabṣirat al-Adilla is not a theological argument but a historical testimony. He names the early imams who preserved and defended Abu Hanifa's method in the eastern lands, from the 2nd/3rd centuries up to his own time. Understanding this chain is crucial for appreciating the school's claim to authentic transmission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage as a historical claim
Notice that Nasafi is not arguing a point of theology here; he is establishing a chain of teachers. Read the Arabic and translation to see the names and places mentioned.
Pay attention to the cities: Marw, Balkh, Samarqand.
2
Identify the chain of transmission
Trace the lineage: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan → Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani → Abu Bakr al-Juzjani → Abu Nasr al-‘Iyadhi. This is the core of the passage.
Muhammad ibn al-Hasan was a direct student of Abu Hanifa.
3
Consider the rhetorical purpose
Nasafi asks: how could Abu Bakr al-Juzjani have arisen after four hundred years? This is to show the early origin of the school and refute those who claim it emerged late.
Reflect on why establishing an early chain is important for authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن أئمة أصحاب أبي حنيفة السالكين طريقه في الأصول والفروع، الناكبين عن الاعتزال في جميع ديار ما وراء النهر وخراسان من مرو وبلخ وغيرهما، كلهم في قديم الزمان كانوا على هذا المذهب، وأئمتنا بسمرقند الجامعون علم الأصول والفروع الذابون عن حريم الدين المناضلون عنه الذين طهر الله تعالى بسبب غزارة علومهم وتبحرهم في علم الكلام، وصلابتهم في الدين، وتشددهم على أهل البدع والضلال الذين صانوا أهل هذه الديار عن أوضار أهل الزيغ والبدع عامة، كانوا على هذا الرأي من لدن أيام الشيخ أبي بكر أحمد بن إسحاق بن صبيح الجوزجاني صاحب أبي سليمان الجوزجاني تلميذ محمد بن الحسن، وكان في أنواع العلوم على الخصوص والعموم في الذروة العالية والرتبة السامية، ومن رأى تصانيفه ككتاب الفرق والتمييز وكتاب التوبة وغيرهما عرف جلالة قدره إلى زماننا هذا. ومن كان صاحب تلميذ محمد بن الحسن كيف يكون ناشئا بعد الأربعمائة ثم تلميذه الشيخ أبو نصر أحمد بن العباس بن الحسين بن جبلة بن طالب بن جابر بن نوفل بن عياض بن يحيى بن قيس بن عبادة الأنصاري سيد الخزرج، كان على هذا الرأي، وهو الذي استشهد في ديار الترك في أيام النصر بن
Then indeed the imams of the companions of Abu Hanifa, those traversing his path in principles and branches, those turning away from Muʿtazilism in all the lands of Transoxiana and Khurasan – from Marw, Balkh, and others – all of them in ancient times were upon this madhhab. And our imams in Samarqand, those who combined the knowledge of principles and branches, the defenders of the sanctity of religion, the fighters for it, whom Allah purified due to the abundance of their sciences and their deep knowledge in the science of kalām, and their firmness in religion, and their severity against the people of innovation and misguidance – those who protected the people of these lands from the filth of the people of deviation and innovation generally – they were upon this opinion from the days of the Shaykh Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ishaq ibn Subayh al-Juzjani, the companion of Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, the student of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. And he was, in the types of sciences specifically and generally, at the highest peak and the lofty rank. And whoever sees his works, such as the book 'al-Furq wa al-Tamyiz' and the book 'al-Tawba' and others, knows the majesty of his rank up to our time. And how can one who is a companion of the student of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan have arisen after four hundred years? Then his student, the Shaykh Abu Nasr Ahmad ibn al-ʿAbbas ibn al-Husayn ibn Jabala ibn Talib ibn Jabir ibn Nawfal ibn ʿIyad ibn Yahya ibn Qays ibn ʿUbada al-Ansari, the master of the Khazraj, was upon this opinion, and he is the one who was martyred in the land of the Turks in the days of al-Nasr ibn...
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage is a historical testimony establishing the continuous transmission of Abu Hanifa's creed from the earliest times. The author begins by stating that the imams among Abu Hanifa's followers, who adhered to his method in both uṣūl (foundations) and furūʿ (branches) and rejected Muʿtazilism throughout Transoxiana and Khurasan (cities like Marw and Balkh), were all upon this madhhab since ancient times. He then focuses on the imams of Samarqand, who were masters of both uṣūl and furūʿ, defenders of the faith, and protectors of the people from innovations. These scholars followed this creed from the time of Shaykh Abu Bakr al-Juzjani, who was a companion of Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, the latter being a student of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani (the companion of Abu Hanifa). The author extols Abu Bakr al-Juzjani's rank and his works. He then poses a rhetorical argument: if Abu Bakr was a companion of a student of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, how could he have arisen after four hundred years? (i.e., the chain is early and authentic). Then he mentions Abu Bakr's student, Abu Nasr al-ʿIyadhi, who was also upon this opinion and was martyred in the land of the Turks. The passage thus provides a direct chain of transmission: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan → Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani → Abu Bakr al-Juzjani → Abu Nasr al-ʿIyadhi, establishing the unbroken continuity of the school.

Key Terms
أئمة
ما وراء النهر
سمرقند
أبو بكر الجوزجاني
أبو سليمان الجوزجاني
أبو نصر العياضي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Maturidi school emerged late without a direct chain back to Abu Hanifa.
Correction: This passage shows a clear teacher-student chain from the 2nd/3rd centuries directly linking Samarqand imams to Abu Hanifa through Muhammad ibn al-Hasan.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who was the direct teacher of Abu Bakr al-Juzjani?
A) Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani
B) Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani
C) Abu Nasr al-‘Iyadhi
D) Abu Hanifa himself

Key Takeaway
Nasafi provides a direct teacher-student chain linking the Maturidi school back to Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, a student of Abu Hanifa.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Nasr al-‘Iyadhi was martyred for his creed. Is your faith something you would sacrifice your life for? What would you change in your daily life to show that you value truth more than comfort?
?
The passage describes scholars who were 'firm in religion and severe against people of innovation'. Are there places in your life where you have allowed innovated practices or beliefs to go unchallenged? What specific step will you take today to correct that?
?
This lesson traces a chain of teachers preserving the creed. Who are the teachers you rely on for your understanding of Aqeedah? Are you ensuring that you are learning from those who are connected to the early generations of Muslims?

The Lineage and Martyrdom of Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi
Describes the lineage and martyrdom of Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the noble lineage and early life of Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi, including his martyrdom and his association with the Maturidi school.

Core Idea
A noble Ansari lineage and early martyrdom marked Abu Nasr as a key Maturidi figure.

This lesson introduces you to Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi, a prominent early figure in the Maturidi tradition. We will learn about his distinguished lineage from the Ansar and his martyrdom in the land of the Turks, which established his credibility and sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about his lineage and martyrdom
Read the Arabic passage once, then follow the translation. Pay attention to the full name and the mention of his martyrdom.
The passage uses a rhetorical question to emphasize his early connection to the tradition.
2
Notice his lineage
Observe that his lineage traces back to the Ansar, specifically the Khazraj tribe, indicating noble ancestry.
3
Reflect on the significance of martyrdom
Consider why being martyred in the land of the Turks adds to his stature as a defender of the truth.
Martyrdom is a high honor in Islamic tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن كان صاحب تلميذ محمد بن الحسن كيف يكون ناشئا بعد الأربعمائة ثم تلميذه الشيخ أبو نصر أحمد بن العباس بن الحسين بن جبلة بن طالب بن جابر بن نوفل بن عياض بن يحيى بن قيس بن عبادة الأنصاري سيد الخزرج، كان على هذا الرأي، وهو الذي استشهد في ديار الترك في أيام النصر بن. وما أتى فيه من الدلائل على صحة قول أهل الحق وبطلان قول المعتزلة والنجارية عرف تبحره في ذلك. وحكي عن الشيخ أبي القاسم الحكيم السمرقندي - رحمه الله - أنه قال: ما أتى الفقيه أبا نصر العياضي أحد من أهل البدع والأهواء وأولي الجدال والمراء في الدين بآية من القرآن يحتج بها عليه لمذهبه إلا تلقاها مبتدها بما يفحمه ويقطعه. وحكي أن رياسة العلماء والدرس كانا إليه وهو ابن اثنتا وعشرين سنة، وحكي أنه لما استشهد خلف أربعين رجلا من أصحابه كانوا من أقران الشيخ أبي منصور الماتريدي والشيخ الحكيم أبي القاسم.
And how can one who was the companion of a student of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan be a beginner after four hundred [years]? Then his student, Sheikh Abu Nasr Ahmad ibn al-Abbas ibn al-Husayn ibn Jabala ibn Talib ibn Jabir ibn Nawfal ibn 'Iyad ibn Yahya ibn Qays ibn 'Ubada al-Ansari, the master of the Khazraj, was upon this opinion, and he is the one who was martyred in the land of the Turks in the days of al-Nasr ibn... And whatever proofs he brought therein for the correctness of the statement of the people of truth and the falsehood of the statement of the Mu'tazila and the Najjariyya, one would know his deep knowledge in that. And it was narrated from Sheikh Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim al-Samarqandi - may Allah have mercy on him - that he said: No one from the people of innovation and desires and those given to argumentation and disputation in religion came to the faqih Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi with a verse from the Quran by which he argued for his madhhab, except that he (al-'Iyadi) received it from its beginning with what silenced him and cut him off. And it was narrated that the leadership of the scholars and teaching were placed upon him while he was twenty-two years old, and it was narrated that when he was martyred, he left behind forty men from his companions who were peers of Sheikh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and Sheikh al-Hakim Abu al-Qasim.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi, emphasizing his noble lineage (descended from Ansar, master of Khazraj) and his adherence to the same opinion (i.e., the Maturidi position). It notes his martyrdom in the land of the Turks. Then it highlights his scholarly depth: anyone who saw the proofs he presented for the truth of the people of truth and the falsehood of the Mu'tazila and Najjariyya would recognize his mastery. A narration from Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim al-Samarqandi testifies that no heretic could argue against him using a Quranic verse without being silenced by al-'Iyadi's response from the beginning. The passage also mentions that al-'Iyadi assumed leadership of scholars and teaching at the age of twenty-two, and that he left behind forty companions who were peers of Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim, indicating his high status and the quality of his students.

Key Terms
أبو نصر العياضي
استشهد
الأنصاري

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Khazraj

Key Takeaway
Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi was a noble Ansari scholar who was martyred in defense of the truth, cementing his place in early Maturidi history.

The Proof from Abu Ahmad's Adherence
Argument that Abu Ahmad's adherence proves madhhab's truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the integrity of a follower can serve as evidence for the truth of a madhhab.

Core Idea
A scholar's character can validate a school of thought.

This passage presents a unique argument: the fact that the virtuous scholar Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi adhered to the madhhab of Abu Hanifa is taken as proof of its correctness. We'll examine this reasoning and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Pay attention to the phrase 'الدليل على صحة مذهب أبي حنيفة'.
2
Identify the argument
Notice how Sheikh Abu Hafs al-Najjari states that the proof is that Abu Ahmad believes in the madhhab. He adds that Abu Ahmad would never believe in a false madhhab.
This is an argument from authority based on Abu Ahmad's character.
3
Reflect on the underlying assumption
Ask yourself: What does this argument assume about Abu Ahmad? It assumes that his judgment and integrity are so sound that his adherence guarantees the truth of the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ابناه الإمامان أبو أحمد وأبو بكر، وهما ممن لا يبلغ الوصف وإن أطنب فيه غاية فضلهما وكنه قدرهما، وقد قال الشيخ أبو حفص العجل النجاري حافد الشيخ أبي حفص الكبير - رحمه الله - وهو كان صدر فقهاء ما وراء النهر وخراسان الدليل على صحة مذهب أبي حنيفة أن أبا أحمد العياضي يعتقد مذهبه، وهو ما كان يعتقد مذهبا باطلا. وروي عن الشيخ أبي القاسم الحكيم أنه قال: ما خرجت خراسان ولا ما وراء النهر منذ مائة سنة مثل الفقيه أبي أحمد العياضي علما وفقها ولسانا ويدا وبيانا ونزاهة وعفة وتقى. فقيل له يرحمك الله، ومن كان يضاهيه قبل هذه المائة سنة؟ فجعل يذكر طبقات العلماء والفقهاء والبلغاء والفصحاء بها إلى يومه فلم يجد.
Then his two sons, the two imams Abu Ahmad and Abu Bakr, are among those whom description cannot reach, even if one goes on at length about the utmost of their virtue and the reality of their status. And Sheikh Abu Hafs al-'Ajl al-Najjari, the grandson of Sheikh Abu Hafs al-Kabir - may Allah have mercy on him - said, and he was the foremost of the jurists of Transoxiana and Khurasan: The proof of the correctness of the madhhab of Abu Hanifa is that Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi believes in his madhhab, and he would never believe in a false madhhab. And it is narrated from Sheikh Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim that he said: Khurasan and Transoxiana have not produced in a hundred years anyone like the faqih Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi in knowledge, jurisprudence, eloquence, action, clarity, purity, chastity, and piety. So it was said to him: May Allah have mercy on you, who was equal to him before this hundred years? So he began to mention the classes of scholars, jurists, eloquent speakers, and fluent orators there until his day, and he did not find [anyone like him].
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage presents testimonies about the two sons of Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi: Abu Ahmad and Abu Bakr. It states that their virtue is indescribable. Then it quotes Sheikh Abu Hafs al-Najjari, a prominent jurist, who argues that the very fact that Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi follows the madhhab of Abu Hanifa is proof of its correctness, because Abu Ahmad would never follow a false madhhab. This is a logical argument from authority: a person of such high caliber would not adhere to an erroneous school. Next, a narration from Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim says that Khurasan and Transoxiana have not produced anyone like Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi in a hundred years, listing many attributes. When asked who rivaled him before that century, the narrator says that Abu al-Qasim started going through the ranks of scholars, jurists, and eloquent speakers up to his own time and found no one comparable.

Key Terms
أبو أحمد العياضي
أبو حفص العجل النجاري
الدليل على صحة مذهب أبي حنيفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is circular or relies on blind following.
Correction: It is an appeal to authority based on the known integrity and scholarship of Abu Ahmad, not blind taqlid. The argument assumes that a person of his stature would only follow what he knows to be true.

Checkpoint
According to Sheikh Abu Hafs al-Najjari, what is the proof of the correctness of Abu Hanifa's madhhab?
A) That many scholars followed it
B) That Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi believed in it
C) That it is supported by hadith
D) That it is the oldest madhhab

Key Takeaway
The integrity of a follower can be a proof of the truth of a madhhab.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the unspoken assumption in this argument: that a virtuous person would never follow a false path. Where in your own life have you trusted someone's character as a guarantee of truth? Was that trust ever misplaced? What does that reveal about the limitations of arguments from authority?
?
Abu Ahmad's adherence is used as evidence for the truth of a madhhab. Think about the scholars you follow—whether in aqeedah, fiqh, or daily life. Is your own adherence based on their personal integrity alone, or have you personally verified the evidence? What is one thing you could do today to move from blind acceptance to conviction?

The Unparalleled Scholar: Testimony of Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim
Praise of Abu Ahmad as unmatched in a century.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate the high regard for Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi as expressed by his peers.

Core Idea
Abu Ahmad was considered unparalleled in a century.

The second testimony comes from Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim, who declares that no one like Abu Ahmad had emerged in a hundred years. This lesson explores the attributes he lists and the search for a comparable figure.

Guided Path
1
Read the testimony
Read the Arabic passage and translation focusing on the attributes mentioned by Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim.
Notice the list: knowledge, jurisprudence, eloquence, action, clarity, purity, chastity, piety.
2
Analyze the method of comparison
When asked about earlier scholars, Abu al-Qasim begins to go through the ranks of scholars, jurists, and eloquent speakers, but finds no equal to Abu Ahmad.
This emphasizes the rarity of his combination of qualities.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider what this testimony reveals about the status of Abu Ahmad and the standards of scholarship in that era.

ثم ابناه الإمامان أبو أحمد وأبو بكر، وهما ممن لا يبلغ الوصف وإن أطنب فيه غاية فضلهما وكنه قدرهما، وقد قال الشيخ أبو حفص العجل النجاري حافد الشيخ أبي حفص الكبير - رحمه الله - وهو كان صدر فقهاء ما وراء النهر وخراسان الدليل على صحة مذهب أبي حنيفة أن أبا أحمد العياضي يعتقد مذهبه، وهو ما كان يعتقد مذهبا باطلا. وروي عن الشيخ أبي القاسم الحكيم أنه قال: ما خرجت خراسان ولا ما وراء النهر منذ مائة سنة مثل الفقيه أبي أحمد العياضي علما وفقها ولسانا ويدا وبيانا ونزاهة وعفة وتقى. فقيل له يرحمك الله، ومن كان يضاهيه قبل هذه المائة سنة؟ فجعل يذكر طبقات العلماء والفقهاء والبلغاء والفصحاء بها إلى يومه فلم يجد.
Then his two sons, the two imams Abu Ahmad and Abu Bakr, are among those whom description cannot reach, even if one goes on at length about the utmost of their virtue and the reality of their status. And Sheikh Abu Hafs al-'Ajl al-Najjari, the grandson of Sheikh Abu Hafs al-Kabir - may Allah have mercy on him - said, and he was the foremost of the jurists of Transoxiana and Khurasan: The proof of the correctness of the madhhab of Abu Hanifa is that Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi believes in his madhhab, and he would never believe in a false madhhab. And it is narrated from Sheikh Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim that he said: Khurasan and Transoxiana have not produced in a hundred years anyone like the faqih Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi in knowledge, jurisprudence, eloquence, action, clarity, purity, chastity, and piety. So it was said to him: May Allah have mercy on you, who was equal to him before this hundred years? So he began to mention the classes of scholars, jurists, eloquent speakers, and fluent orators there until his day, and he did not find [anyone like him].
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage presents testimonies about the two sons of Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi: Abu Ahmad and Abu Bakr. It states that their virtue is indescribable. Then it quotes Sheikh Abu Hafs al-Najjari, a prominent jurist, who argues that the very fact that Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi follows the madhhab of Abu Hanifa is proof of its correctness, because Abu Ahmad would never follow a false madhhab. This is a logical argument from authority: a person of such high caliber would not adhere to an erroneous school. Next, a narration from Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim says that Khurasan and Transoxiana have not produced anyone like Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi in a hundred years, listing many attributes. When asked who rivaled him before that century, the narrator says that Abu al-Qasim started going through the ranks of scholars, jurists, and eloquent speakers up to his own time and found no one comparable.

Key Terms
أبو أحمد العياضي
أبو القاسم الحكيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This testimony is mere flattery or exaggeration.
Correction: It is a serious statement from a major scholar, supported by a systematic search through historical figures, indicating a well-considered judgment.

Checkpoint
What did Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim do when asked about scholars before the hundred-year period?
A) He named several scholars equal to Abu Ahmad
B) He mentioned the classes of scholars and found no one like him
C) He said Abu Ahmad was the best in every field
D) He refused to answer

Key Takeaway
Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi was regarded as uniquely excellent in a broad range of qualities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Ahmad was praised for combining knowledge, action, eloquence, purity, chastity, and piety. Which of these eight attributes do you most neglect in your own life, and what one step will you take today to begin developing it?
?
If someone were to search for a person like you among your peers, what would they find? In light of this testimony, what kind of legacy do you want to leave, and how can you start building it now?
?
The speaker could not find anyone equal to Abu Ahmad after a thorough search across a century. Do you know anyone today who embodies all these virtues? If not, what does that reveal about your own priorities and the standards you set for yourself?

Life of Imam al-Nasafi Maturidi
beginner
4 min
The 'Iyadi Family and the Ten Issues
Nasafi praises the 'Iyadi scholars and introduces the ten issues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key role of the al-'Iyadi family in defending the Maturidi school and the nature of the ten issues that define the Maturidi-Mu'tazila debate.

Core Idea
The al-'Iyadi family were intellectual pillars of Maturidi orthodoxy.

This passage from Nasafi's Tabirat al-Adilla introduces us to the scholarly lineage of the Maturidi school in Samarqand. It centers on the al-'Iyadi family, especially Abu Nasr and his sons Abu Ahmad and Abu Bakr, who were renowned for their defense of Sunni doctrine against the Mu'tazila. The passage culminates by naming the famous 'ten issues' (al-masa'il al-'ashar) that encapsulate the core points of disagreement between the two schools.

Guided Path
1
Read the praise of Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi
Notice how he is described as able to refute any scriptural argument from innovators.
His leadership at age 22 is highlighted.
2
Note the virtues of his sons, Abu Ahmad and Abu Bakr
They are portrayed as incomparable imams, with Abu Ahmad's adherence to Abu Hanifa's school used as proof of its correctness.
Abu Bakr's final advice emphasizes Ahl al-Sunna.
3
Identify the ten issues (al-masa'il al-'ashar)
The passage names these as the foundational points of dispute between the Maturidis and the Mu'tazila.
They are called the 'Iyadiyya issues after the family.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما أتى فيه من الدلائل على صحة قول أهل الحق وبطلان قول المعتزلة والنجارية عرف تبحره في ذلك.
وحكي عن الشيخ أبي القاسم الحكيم السمرقندي - رحمه الله - أنه قال: ما أتى الفقيه أبا نصر العياضي أحد من أهل البدع والأهواء وأولي الجدال والمراء في الدين بآية من القرآن يحتج بها عليه لمذهبه إلا تلقاها مبتدها بما يفحمه ويقطعه وحكي أن رياسة العلماء والدرس كانا إليه وهو ابن اثنتا وعشرين سنة، وحكي أنه لما استشهد خلف أربعين رجلا من أصحابه كانوا من أقران الشيخ أبي منصور الماتريدي والشيخ الحكيم أبي القاسم ثم ابناه الإمامان أبو أحمد وأبو بكر، وهما ممن لا يبلغ الوصف وإن أطنب فيه غاية فضلهما وكنه قدرهما، وقد قال الشيخ أبو حفص العجل النجاري حافد الشيخ أبي حفص الكبير
—
رحمه الله
وهو كان صدر
فقهاء ما وراء النهر وخراسان الدليل على صحة مذهب أبي حنيفة أن أبا أحمد العياضي يعتقد مذهبه ، وهو ما كان يعتقد مذهبا باطلا.
وروي عن الشيخ أبي القاسم الحكيم أنه قال : ما خرجت خراسان ولا ما وراء النهر منذ مائة سنة مثل الفقيه أبي أحمد العياضي علما وفقها ولسانا ويدا وبيانا ونزاهة وعفة وتقى. فقيل له يرحمك الله، ومن كان يضاهيه قبل هذه المائة سنة؟ فجعل يذكر طبقات العلماء والفقهاء والبلغاء والفصحاء بها إلى يومه فلم يجد
في كافتهم ممن يقرن به فيماثله، أو يقاس به فيعاد له، وكذا أخوه أبو بكر كان يدانيه في أنواع العلوم وأسباب الشرف والفضل، وهو الذي أوصى أهل سمرقند عند انقضاء أجله أن يتمسكوا بمذهب أهل السنة ويتجانبوا الأهواء والبدع خصوصا الاعتزال، وجميع المسائل العشر التي هي المسائل العشر التي هي أصول المسائل الخلافية بيننا وبين المعتزلة وهي المعروفة بالمسائل العشر العياضية.
وقبل هذه الطبقة كان القاضي أبو عبد الله محمد بن أسلم بن سلمة بن عبد الله ابن المغيرة بن عمرو بن عوف بن حاضر الأزدي على هذا الرأي، وكان على قضاء سمرقند قند في أيام نصر بن أحمد الكبير، وهو الأمير نصر بن أحمد بن أسد ابن سامان ثم إنه توفى يوم الاثنين لثمان عشرة مضت من شهر ربيع الآخر من شهور سنة ثمان وستين ومائتين، وصير الأمير نصر بن أحمد ابنه إسماعيل على المظالم مكان أبيه يوم الأربعاء بعد وفاة أبيه بعشرة أيام.
ومن هذه الطبقة بسمرقند أبو بكر محمد بن اليمان السمرقندي صاحب كتاب معالم الدين وكتاب الاعتصام وغيرهما من الكتب في الكلام، وله كتاب الرد على الكرامية من رآه عرف تبحره في الكلام وجلالة قدره في العلم بأصول الدين وظني أنه أول من رد مذاهب الكرامية إذ كانت نبعت في زمانه.
وبعد هؤلاء الفقيه أبو سلمة محمد بن محمد صاحب كتاب جمل أصول الدين وكان تخرج على الفقيه أبي أحمد العياضي وأخذ منه الفقه والكلام.
والشيخ أبو الحسن الرستغفني صحاب كتاب إرشاد المهتدي وغيره من
And what he brought in it of proofs for the correctness of the statement of the people of truth and the falsehood of the statement of the Mu'tazila and al-Najjariyya, one recognized his profundity in that. And it was narrated from Sheikh Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim al-Samarqandi - may Allah have mercy on him - that he said: 'Not a single person from the people of innovation and desires and the people of argumentation and disputation in religion came to the faqih Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi with a verse of the Qur'an that he used as proof for his school, except that he received it from its beginning in a way that silenced and cut him off.' And it was narrated that the leadership of scholars and teaching was in his hands while he was twenty-two years old. And it was narrated that when he was martyred, he left behind forty men from his companions who were peers of Sheikh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and Sheikh al-Hakim Abu al-Qasim, then his two sons, the two imams Abu Ahmad and Abu Bakr, and they are among those whose description cannot be reached, even if one expounds at length on the utmost of their virtue and the reality of their status. And Sheikh Abu Hafs al-'Ijl al-Najjari, the grandson of Sheikh Abu Hafs al-Kabir, said: 'And he was the foremost of the jurists of Transoxiana and Khurasan. The proof of the correctness of the school of Abu Hanifa is that Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi believed in his school, and he would not believe in a false school.' And it was narrated from Sheikh Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim that he said: 'Khurasan and Transoxiana have not produced in a hundred years anyone like the faqih Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi in knowledge, jurisprudence, tongue, hand, eloquence, purity, chastity, and piety.' It was said to him: 'May Allah have mercy on you, who resembled him before this hundred years?' So he began to mention the layers of scholars, jurists, eloquent speakers, and rhetoricians in them up to his day, and he did not find among all of them anyone who equaled him to match him, or could be compared to him to be his equivalent. Likewise, his brother Abu Bakr was his equal in types of sciences and causes of honor and virtue, and he is the one who advised the people of Samarqand at the end of his life to adhere to the school of Ahl al-Sunna and avoid desires and innovations, especially i'tizal (Mu'tazilism), and all the ten issues - which are the ten issues that are the foundations of the disputatious issues between us and the Mu'tazila - and they are known as the ten 'Iyadiyya issues. And before this layer was the Qadi Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Aslam ibn Salama ibn 'Abd Allah ibn al-Mughira ibn 'Amr ibn 'Awf ibn Hadir al-Azdi upon this opinion, and he was the qadi of Samarqand in the days of Nasr ibn Ahmad al-Kabir, who is the Amir Nasr ibn Ahmad ibn Asad ibn Saman. Then he died on Monday, the 18th of Rabi' al-Akhir of the year 268 AH, and the Amir Nasr ibn Ahmad appointed his son Isma'il over the grievances (mazalim) in place of his father on Wednesday, ten days after his father's death. And from this layer in Samarqand is Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Yaman al-Samarqandi, the author of the book Ma'alim al-Din and the book al-I'tisam and other books on kalam, and he has the book al-Radd 'ala al-Karramiyya. Whoever saw it recognized his profundity in kalam and his great status in the science of usul al-din. And I think that he was the first to refute the schools of the Karramiyya since it had emerged in his time. And after these, the faqih Abu Salama Muhammad ibn Muhammad, the author of the book Jumal Usul al-Din, and he graduated under the faqih Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi and took from him fiqh and kalam. And Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani, the author of the book Irshad al-Muhtadi and others of
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage is a historical-biographical account that traces the scholarly lineage of the Maturidi school in Samarqand and introduces the famous 'ten issues' (al-masa'il al-'ashar) that distinguish the school from the Mu'tazila. The author begins by highlighting the depth of proofs presented earlier against the Mu'tazila and Najjariyya. He then quotes Sheikh Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim al-Samarqandi praising the prowess of the faqih Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi, who could refute any scriptural argument of innovators. It is also noted that al-'Iyadi became a leading scholar and teacher at age twenty-two. Upon his martyrdom, he left forty disciples who were contemporaries of Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and al-Hakim Abu al-Qasim. His two sons, Abu Ahmad and Abu Bakr, are praised as imams of unmatched virtue. Sheikh Abu Hafs al-Najjari adds that Abu Ahmad's adherence to the school of Abu Hanifa itself proves the correctness of that school. Another report from al-Hakim praises Abu Ahmad as unparalleled in a century in knowledge, jurisprudence, eloquence, and piety. When asked about his predecessors, al-Hakim could find no equal. Then the passage mentions that Abu Ahmad's brother Abu Bakr was his peer, and that Abu Bakr's final advice to the people of Samarqand was to adhere to Ahl al-Sunna and avoid innovation, especially Mu'tazilism, and to uphold the ten issues (al-masa'il al-'ashar) that are the foundational points of difference between the Maturidis and the Mu'tazila. These issues are called al-masa'il al-'ashar al-'Iyadiyya. The account then goes to earlier scholars: Qadi Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Aslam al-Azdi, who was a qadi of Samarqand during the reign of Amir Nasr ibn Ahmad. He died in 268 AH, after which the amir appointed his son Isma'il over the mazalim. Also from this earlier period is Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Yaman al-Samarqandi, a prolific author in kalam, known for his refutation of the Karramiyya, being perhaps the first to do so. After these, the faqih Abu Salama Muhammad ibn Muhammad, a student of Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi, wrote the book Jumal Usul al-Din. Finally, Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani is mentioned as the author of Irshad al-Muhtadi and other works. Throughout, the passage emphasizes the continuity of Sunni scholarship in Samarqand and the central role of the ten issues in defending orthodoxy against Mu'tazilism.

Key Terms
المسائل العشر
المسائل العشر العياضية
أبو نصر العياضي
أبو أحمد العياضي
أبو بكر العياضي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Abu Bakr al-'Iyadi advise the people of Samarqand at his death?
A) To follow the school of the Mu'tazila
B) To adhere to the school of Ahl al-Sunna and avoid innovation, especially i'tizal
C) To abandon kalam and focus only on fiqh
D) To emigrate from Samarqand

Key Takeaway
The 'Iyadi family were central to early Maturidi scholarship, and the ten issues (al-masa'il al-'ashar) are the key points of dispute with the Mu'tazila.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does the fact that Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi's belief in a school is given as proof of its correctness challenge your own basis for which school of thought you follow? Do you follow because of the authority of scholars or have you investigated yourself?
?
The passage says Abu Bakr advised to adhere to Ahl al-Sunna and avoid innovations. Examine your own beliefs: are you truly adhering to the Sunnah, or have you unknowingly adopted something from desires?
?
When you hear such high praise of scholars, do you feel inspired to learn more or do you become complacent, thinking 'I am not like them'? What would it mean for you to learn from their example even in your current situation?

Early and Later Maturidi Scholars in Samarqand
Nasafi lists earlier and later Maturidi scholars in Samarqand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the continuity of Maturidi scholarship in Samarqand through key figures such as Qadi Abu Abd Allah, Abu Bakr al-Yaman, Abu Salama, and Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani.

Core Idea
Maturidi scholarship in Samarqand was a continuous tradition passed through generations.

This second part of the biographical passage traces the scholarly lineage beyond the 'Iyadi family, mentioning earlier and later scholars who upheld the Maturidi school. It highlights the role of Qadi Abu Abd Allah al-Azdi, the prolific writer Abu Bakr al-Yaman (who refuted the Karramiyya), and the later scholars Abu Salama and Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani, showing a rich intellectual heritage.

Guided Path
1
Read about Qadi Abu Abd Allah al-Azdi
He was a qadi of Samarqand during the reign of Amir Nasr ibn Ahmad and died in 268 AH.
His appointment to mazalim after death is noted.
2
Learn about Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Yaman
He wrote several kalam books including a refutation of the Karramiyya, and is thought to be the first to do so.
His work Ma'alim al-Din and al-I'tisam are mentioned.
3
Note the later scholars Abu Salama and Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani
Abu Salama was a student of Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi and wrote Jumal Usul al-Din. Abu al-Hasan wrote Irshad al-Muhtadi.

And it was narrated that the leadership of scholars and teaching was in his hands while he was twenty-two years old. And it was narrated that when he was martyred, he left behind forty men from his companions who were peers of Sheikh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and Sheikh al-Hakim Abu al-Qasim, then his two sons, the two imams Abu Ahmad and Abu Bakr, and they are among those whose description cannot be reached, even if one expounds at length on the utmost of their virtue and the reality of their status. And Sheikh Abu Hafs al-'Ijl al-Najjari, the grandson of Sheikh Abu Hafs al-Kabir, said: 'And he was the foremost of the jurists of Transoxiana and Khurasan. The proof of the correctness of the school of Abu Hanifa is that Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi believed in his school, and he would not believe in a false school.' And it was narrated from Sheikh Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim that he said: 'Khurasan and Transoxiana have not produced in a hundred years anyone like the faqih Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi in knowledge, jurisprudence, tongue, hand, eloquence, purity, chastity, and piety.' It was said to him: 'May Allah have mercy on you, who resembled him before this hundred years?' So he began to mention the layers of scholars, jurists, eloquent speakers, and rhetoricians in them up to his day, and he did not find among all of them anyone who equaled him to match him, or could be compared to him to be his equivalent. Likewise, his brother Abu Bakr was his equal in types of sciences and causes of honor and virtue, and he is the one who advised the people of Samarqand at the end of his life to adhere to the school of Ahl al-Sunna and avoid desires and innovations, especially i'tizal (Mu'tazilism), and all the ten issues - which are the ten issues that are the foundations of the disputatious issues between us and the Mu'tazila - and they are known as the ten 'Iyadiyya issues. And before this layer was the Qadi Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Aslam ibn Salama ibn 'Abd Allah ibn al-Mughira ibn 'Amr ibn 'Awf ibn Hadir al-Azdi upon this opinion, and he was the qadi of Samarqand in the days of Nasr ibn Ahmad al-Kabir, who is the Amir Nasr ibn Ahmad ibn Asad ibn Saman. Then he died on Monday, the 18th of Rabi' al-Akhir of the year 268 AH, and the Amir Nasr ibn Ahmad appointed his son Isma'il over the grievances (mazalim) in place of his father on Wednesday, ten days after his father's death. And from this layer in Samarqand is Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Yaman al-Samarqandi, the author of the book Ma'alim al-Din and the book al-I'tisam and other books on kalam, and he has the book al-Radd 'ala al-Karramiyya. Whoever saw it recognized his profundity in kalam and his great status in the science of usul al-din. And I think that he was the first to refute the schools of the Karramiyya since it had emerged in his time. And after these, the faqih Abu Salama Muhammad ibn Muhammad, the author of the book Jumal Usul al-Din, and he graduated under the faqih Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi and took from him fiqh and kalam. And Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani, the author of the book Irshad al-Muhtadi and others of
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage is a historical-biographical account that traces the scholarly lineage of the Maturidi school in Samarqand and introduces the famous 'ten issues' (al-masa'il al-'ashar) that distinguish the school from the Mu'tazila. The author begins by highlighting the depth of proofs presented earlier against the Mu'tazila and Najjariyya. He then quotes Sheikh Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim al-Samarqandi praising the prowess of the faqih Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi, who could refute any scriptural argument of innovators. It is also noted that al-'Iyadi became a leading scholar and teacher at age twenty-two. Upon his martyrdom, he left forty disciples who were contemporaries of Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and al-Hakim Abu al-Qasim. His two sons, Abu Ahmad and Abu Bakr, are praised as imams of unmatched virtue. Sheikh Abu Hafs al-Najjari adds that Abu Ahmad's adherence to the school of Abu Hanifa itself proves the correctness of that school. Another report from al-Hakim praises Abu Ahmad as unparalleled in a century in knowledge, jurisprudence, eloquence, and piety. When asked about his predecessors, al-Hakim could find no equal. Then the passage mentions that Abu Ahmad's brother Abu Bakr was his peer, and that Abu Bakr's final advice to the people of Samarqand was to adhere to Ahl al-Sunna and avoid innovation, especially Mu'tazilism, and to uphold the ten issues (al-masa'il al-'ashar) that are the foundational points of difference between the Maturidis and the Mu'tazila. These issues are called al-masa'il al-'ashar al-'Iyadiyya. The account then goes to earlier scholars: Qadi Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Aslam al-Azdi, who was a qadi of Samarqand during the reign of Amir Nasr ibn Ahmad. He died in 268 AH, after which the amir appointed his son Isma'il over the mazalim. Also from this earlier period is Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Yaman al-Samarqandi, a prolific author in kalam, known for his refutation of the Karramiyya, being perhaps the first to do so. After these, the faqih Abu Salama Muhammad ibn Muhammad, a student of Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi, wrote the book Jumal Usul al-Din. Finally, Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani is mentioned as the author of Irshad al-Muhtadi and other works. Throughout, the passage emphasizes the continuity of Sunni scholarship in Samarqand and the central role of the ten issues in defending orthodoxy against Mu'tazilism.

Key Terms
القاضي أبو عبد الله محمد بن أسلم
أبو بكر محمد بن اليمان
أبو سلمة محمد بن محمد
أبو الحسن الرستغفني
الكرامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Yaman
C) Abu Salama Muhammad ibn Muhammad

Key Takeaway
Maturidi scholarship in Samarqand was maintained by a chain of notable scholars, including the first refuter of the Karramiyya.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Karramiyya emerged in the time of Abu Bakr al-Samarqandi, and he took up his pen to refute them. What false beliefs or ideologies are spreading around you today that you are passively ignoring? Which of your talents could you use to defend the truth, and what is one concrete step you will take this week to educate yourself so you can respond?
?
Scholars like Qadi al-Azdi and Abu Bakr al-Samarqandi are remembered for their works and roles in preserving orthodoxy. Your life will end—what will you leave behind? Are you investing in knowledge that will outlast you, or are you consumed by fleeting distractions? Write down one legacy of Islamic learning you can begin building today.
?
The faqih Abu Salama 'graduated under' a specific teacher. Do you know the chain of scholars through whom your own Islamic knowledge has reached you? If not, find out. If you have no such chain, ask yourself: what am I doing to ensure my faith is rooted in authentic, transmitted knowledge rather than personal opinion?

Qadi Abu Abdullah: An Early Maturidi Judge
Biographical notice of Qadi Abu Abdullah in Samarkand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of Qadi Abu Abdullah as an early Maturidi scholar and judge in Samarkand, and his connection to the Nasrid dynasty.

Core Idea
The scholarly lineage of Maturidism began with authoritative judges like Qadi Abu Abdullah.

The passage begins by introducing one of the earliest Maturidi figures, Qadi Abu Abdullah, who served as a judge in Samarkand under Prince Nasr ibn Ahmad. This biographical notice establishes the historical roots of the Maturidi school in the region. By examining his life, we see how early Maturidi scholars were also community leaders.

Guided Path
1
Read the lineage and position
Read the Arabic carefully to see the full name and title of Qadi Abu Abdullah. Notice his role as judge (qadi) and the ruling prince.
The lineage is given in full, showing the importance of ancestry.
2
Note the death date
Identify the precise date of his death: Monday, 18 Rabi' al-Akhir 268 AH. This helps place him historically.
3
Understand the political context
Read about how his son was appointed to handle grievances (mazalim) by the prince after his death, showing continuity of leadership.
This ties the scholar to the Samanid administration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقبل هذه الطبقة كان القاضي أبو عبد الله محمد بن أسلم بن سلمة بن عبد الله ابن المغيرة بن عمرو بن عوف بن حاضر الأزدي على هذا الرأي، وكان على قضاء سمرقند في أيام نصر بن أحمد الكبير، وهو الأمير نصر بن أحمد بن أسد ابن سامان ثم إنه توفى يوم الاثنين لثمان عشرة مضت من شهر ربيع الآخر من شهور سنة ثمان وستين ومائتين، وصير الأمير نصر بن أحمد ابنه إسماعيل على المظالم مكان أبيه يوم الأربعاء بعد وفاة أبيه بعشرة أيام.
ومن هذه الطبقة بسمرقند أبو بكر محمد بن اليمان السمرقندي صاحب كتاب معالم الدين وكتاب الاعتصام وغيرهما من الكتب في الكلام، وله كتاب الرد على الكرامية من رآه عرف تبحره في الكلام وجلالة قدره في العلم بأصول الدين وظني أنه أول من رد مذاهب الكرامية إذ كانت نبعت في زمانه.
وبعد هؤلاء الفقيه أبو سلمة محمد بن محمد صاحب كتاب جمل أصول الدين وكان تخرج على الفقيه أبي أحمد العياضي وأخذ منه الفقه والكلام.
والشيخ أبو الحسن الرستغفني صاحب كتاب إرشاد المهتدي وغيره من الكتب في الكلام، وكتاب الزوائد والفوائد في أصناف العلوم
Before this generation was the judge Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Aslam ibn Salama ibn Abdullah ibn al-Mughira ibn Amr ibn Awf ibn Hadir al-Azdi upon this view, and he was the judge of Samarkand in the days of Nasr ibn Ahmad the Great, who is the prince Nasr ibn Ahmad ibn Asad ibn Saman. Then he died on Monday, eighteen days having passed of the month Rabi' al-Akhir of the months of the year 268 [AH], and the prince Nasr ibn Ahmad made his son Isma'il in charge of grievances in place of his father on Wednesday, ten days after his father's death. And from this generation in Samarkand was Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Yaman al-Samarqandi, author of the book Ma'alim al-Din and the book al-I'tisam and other books on kalam, and he has the book al-Radd 'ala al-Karramiyya; whoever sees it knows his deep knowledge in kalam and his great status in knowledge of the principles of religion, and I think he is the first to refute the doctrines of the Karramiyya since they had emerged in his time. And after these, the faqih Abu Salama Muhammad ibn Muhammad, author of the book Jumal Usul al-Din, and he graduated under the faqih Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi and took from him fiqh and kalam. And Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani, author of the book Irshad al-Muhtadi and other books on kalam, and the book al-Zawa'id wa al-Fawa'id in various sciences.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage provides biographical details of several early Maturidi scholars in Samarkand. It begins with Qadi Abu Abdullah, giving his full lineage and noting his tenure as judge under Prince Nasr ibn Ahmad, along with his death date in 268 AH. It then transitions to Abu Bakr al-Samarqandi, highlighting his works and specifically his refutation of the Karramiyya sect; the author asserts that al-Samarqandi was the first to refute them, as the Karramiyya emerged in his time. Next, Abu Salama is mentioned as a student of Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi and author of Jumal Usul al-Din. Finally, al-Rustughfani is noted for his works on kalam. The passage underscores the scholarly productivity and orthodoxy of these figures.

Abu Bakr al-Samarqandi and the Refutation of the Karramiyya
Biographical notices of three Maturidi scholars and the refutation of Karramiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of Abu Bakr al-Samarqandi's refutation of the Karramiyya sect and the contributions of later scholars Abu Salama and al-Rustughfani to Maturidi theology.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr al-Samarqandi was the first to systematically refute the Karramiyya, defending Sunni orthodoxy.

This lesson introduces three key Maturidi scholars from Samarkand: Abu Bakr al-Samarqandi, who authored important works including a refutation of the Karramiyya; Abu Salama, who wrote Jumal Usul al-Din; and al-Rustughfani, known for his kalam writings. Their efforts illustrate the early Maturidi commitment to defending and systematizing Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify Abu Bakr al-Samarqandi and his works
Read the second paragraph. Note the list of his books: Ma'alim al-Din, al-I'tisam, and especially al-Radd 'ala al-Karramiyya. Understand that he was a prolific author in kalam.
The author thinks he is the first refuter of the Karramiyya.
2
Understand the Karramiyya context
The passage mentions that the Karramiyya emerged in his time. This explains why his refutation was pioneering.
3
Examine Abu Salama and al-Rustughfani
Read the notices for Abu Salama (student of Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi, author of Jumal Usul al-Din) and al-Rustughfani (author of Irshad al-Muhtadi and other kalam works). Note their scholarly lineage.
These scholars continued the Maturidi tradition.

Al-Maturidi: The Master of Sciences and His Legacy
Praise of al-Maturidi and his epitaph

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate the immense scholarly stature of Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi as described by his contemporaries and the epitaph ordered for his grave.

Core Idea
Al-Maturidi's epitaph declares he 'passed through sciences with his breaths'.

This lesson introduces the towering figure of Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, whose mastery of the sciences is celebrated with poetic epitaph. We will examine the praise heaped upon him and the students who graduated under his tutelage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on al-Maturidi's scholarship and epitaph
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the metaphorical language: diving into oceans, extracting pearls.
2
Understand the metaphorical language
The passage uses vivid metaphors to describe his knowledge. Identify phrases like 'ghasa fi buhur al-'ulum' and 'istakhraja durraha'.
3
Identify the students he taught
The passage mentions two students by name: Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi and Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani. Note their titles.
This shows al-Maturidi was not isolated but had a school.
4
Reflect on the epitaph's meaning
The epitaph says he 'passed through sciences with his breaths' and 'exhausted his capacity'. What does that tell you about his dedication?
Consider the phrase 'istnafadha al-wus'a' meaning he used his full capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو لم يكن فيهم إلا الإمام أبو منصور الماتريدي ـ الذي غاص في بحور العلوم واستخرج دررها وأتى حجج الدين فزين بفصاحته وغزارة علومه وجودة قريحته غررها حتى أمر الشيخ أبو القاسم الحكيم أن يكتب على قبره حين توفى: هذا قبر من جاز العلوم بأنفاسه، واستنفذ الوسع في نشره وأقياسه، فحمدت في الدين آثاره واجتنى من عمره ثماره. وهو الذي تخرج عليه الفقيه أبو أحمد العياضي في أنواع العلوم والشيخ أبو الحسن الرستغفني وغيرهما من العلماء المتبحرين في العلوم الملية لكان كافيا وعن ثلب رأي هو لذوي العقول والدين زاجرا، ومن رأى تصانيفه ككتاب التوحيد وكتاب المقالات وكتاب رد أوائل الأدلة للكعبي وكتاب رد تهذيب الجدل للكعبي وكتاب بيان وهم المعتزلة ورد كتاب الكعبي في وعيد الفساق ورد الأصول الخمسة لأبي عمر الباهلي ورد كتاب الإمامة لبعض الروافض وكتابيه في الرد على القرامطة يرد في أحدهما أصول مذاهبهم
And if there had not been among them except the Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi—who dived into the oceans of sciences and extracted their pearls, and brought the proofs of religion and adorned its brilliant points with his eloquence, abundance of his knowledge, and excellence of his intelligence, until Shaykh Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim ordered that be written on his grave when he died: 'This is the grave of one who passed through the sciences with his breaths, and exhausted his capacity in disseminating them and drawing analogies, so his traces were praised in religion and he garnered from his life its fruits.' And he is the one under whom graduated the faqih Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi in various sciences, and Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani, and others from the scholars deeply learned in the religious sciences, would have sufficed, and it would have deterred those with intellect and religion from defaming his opinion. And whoever sees his works such as the Kitab al-Tawhid, and Kitab al-Maqalat, and Kitab Radd Awa'il al-Adilla li al-Ka'bi, and Kitab Radd Tahdhib al-Jadal li al-Ka'bi, and Kitab Bayan Wahm al-Mu'tazila wa Radd Kitab al-Ka'bi fi Wa'id al-Fussaq, and Radd al-Usul al-Khamsa li Abi 'Amr al-Bahili, and Radd Kitab al-Imama li ba'd al-Rawafid, and his two books in refutation of the Qaramita, in one of which he refutes the principles of their doctrines.
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
This passage is a eulogy of Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, praising his profound knowledge and mastery of kalam. It describes his scholarly output using metaphorical language: he dived into the oceans of sciences and extracted pearls, and adorned religion with his eloquence and intelligence. The passage records that Shaykh Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim ordered an epitaph for his grave praising his exhaustive efforts in disseminating and analogical reasoning. It then notes that he was the teacher of prominent scholars like Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi and al-Rustughfani. The author asserts that even if al-Maturidi were the only scholar in that generation, he alone would suffice and deter detractors. Finally, a long list of his works is given, including refutations of the Mu'tazila (especially al-Ka'bi), the Rafida, and the Qaramita, highlighting his role as a defender of Sunni orthodoxy against various deviant groups.

Key Terms
الإمام أبو منصور الماتريدي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Maturidi was a solitary scholar with few students
Correction: He taught prominent scholars like al-'Iyadi and al-Rustughfani.

Checkpoint

D) Al-Ka'bi

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Maturidi was celebrated as a master of sciences, with an epitaph praising his exhaustive scholarly efforts, and he trained notable scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you died today, what would be written on your grave about your pursuit of knowledge? Would it say you 'passed through the sciences with your breaths'?
?
How much of your capacity are you truly exhausting in seeking beneficial knowledge? Is your effort a fraction of al-Maturidi's 'استنفذ الوسع'?
?
Are you grateful to the scholars who taught you, such that you could be counted among their legacy? Do you actively spread what you learn, or do you hoard knowledge?
