Abu Bakr's Financial Sacrifices for Islam
Details Abu Bakr's financial sacrifices and personal risk in Mecca.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extent of Abu Bakr's financial sacrifices for Islam and his complete trust in Allah.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr gave all his wealth for Islam, trusting Allah alone for his family.

This lesson focuses on the first part of the passage where Imam al-Nasafi details Abu Bakr's unparalleled financial support for the Prophet. His actions demonstrate the highest level of generosity and reliance on Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage about Abu Bakr's wealth and assistance to the Prophet during the Meccan period.
Notice the Prophet's statement about Abu Bakr's wealth.
2
Reflect on the giving of all wealth
Consider that he gave all he owned and when asked about his children, he replied 'Allah.'
3
Understand the freeing of the tortured
He used his wealth to free those being tortured by the polytheists and even risked his own life.
This demonstrates complete dedication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إنه في جميع المدة التي أقام رسول الله عليه السلام بمكة بعد المبعث إلى وقت الهجرة وهي ثلاث عشرة سنة كان يعاون النبي عليه السلام بماله حتى قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: 'ما نفعني مال ما نفعني مال أبي بكر' حتى ذكر أنه استعان ببعض ماله فبذل جميع ما كان يملكه فقيل : ما تركت لأولادك قال : الله، ونجى الله بماله المعذبين من أيدي الأعداء وبنفسه، وكان في أيام المواسم يطوف مع النبي عليه السلام على من حج من أشراف القبائل، وكان يذكر محاسن الإسلام بين أيديهم، ويرغبهم في الإسلام ويدعوهم إليه، وعلي الله إذ ذاك صغير لا يؤبه لقوله ولا يقتدى به ولا مال ينفق في نصرة الدين، ثم كان أبو بكر في الجاهلية من أهل الرأي والتدبير كبير الشأن، ولعظم مرتبته في ذلك تبعه من ذكرنا من أكابر الناس وعظماء قريش فأسلموا ببركة سعيه ثم إنه تحمل مدة مقامهم بمكة ما تحمل من أنواع المشاق والشدائد و دروب المكاره والمتاعب، فما فترت في تقوية الدين عزيمته ولا لانت عريكته، ولا اعتراه في أثناء ذلك مع طول مقاساته الشدائد سآمة، ولا أدركته على كثرة الأذى من طبقات العدى ندامة بل ازداد في نصرة الدين كل يوم، وتقوية الرسول وإظهار شعار الملة الحنيفية مضاء في الذب عن رسول رب العزة ومن آمن به واتبعه ممن لا عشيرة له فيستظهر بها ولا رهط يعتصم به كفاية وغناء، ولم يكن يمس من تلك الشدائد عليا الله شيء لصغر سنه ووقوع الأمن للأعداء من أن يكون بسعيه للدين انتشار، ويحصل بدعوته للملة أعوان وأنصار، ولسوابقه البادية
Then indeed, during the entire period that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, stayed in Mecca after the mission until the time of emigration, which was thirteen years, he (Abū Bakr) would assist the Prophet, peace be upon him, with his wealth, until he (the Prophet) said, peace and blessings be upon him: 'No wealth has benefited me as the wealth of Abū Bakr has benefited me.' Until it is mentioned that he sought help from some of his wealth, so he gave all that he owned. So it was said: 'What did you leave for your children?' He said: 'Allah.' And Allah saved with his wealth those who were being tortured from the hands of enemies, and with his own person. And during the seasons (of Hajj) he would go around with the Prophet, peace be upon him, to those who had performed Hajj from the nobles of the tribes, and he would mention the beauties of Islam before them, and would encourage them to Islam and call them to it. And ʿAlī, may Allah be pleased with him, at that time was young, his words were not regarded, nor was he followed, nor did he have wealth to spend in support of the religion. Then Abū Bakr in the pre-Islamic period was among the people of opinion and management, great in status, and due to the greatness of his rank in that, those we mentioned among the great people and nobles of Quraysh followed him, so they embraced Islam by the blessing of his effort. Then he bore during their stay in Mecca all kinds of hardships, severities, difficulties, and troubles. His resolve did not slacken in strengthening the religion, nor did his firmness soften, nor did he become weary during that despite the length of enduring hardships, nor did he feel regret despite the abundance of harm from the classes of enemies; rather, he increased every day in supporting the religion, strengthening the Messenger, and manifesting the symbols of the Ḥanīfī faith. He was determined in defending the Messenger of the Lord of Might and those who believed in him and followed him, from those who had no clan to rely on or company to cling to, with sufficiency and wealth. And none of those hardships touched ʿAlī, may Allah be pleased with him, due to his young age and the safety that the enemies felt from his efforts for the religion spreading and his call gaining supporters and helpers. And (by) his obvious past merits...
Source pages p. 1189

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of Abū Bakr's unparalleled sacrifices and steadfastness in supporting Islam during the Meccan period. It begins by emphasizing that throughout the entire thirteen-year period from the Prophet's mission to the Hijra, Abū Bakr assisted the Prophet with his wealth, to the extent that the Prophet declared that no wealth benefited him as much as Abū Bakr's. He then gave all his wealth, and when asked what he left for his children, he simply replied 'Allah,' indicating complete trust in God. Moreover, he used his wealth to free those being tortured by the polytheists, and also risked his own life. During the Hajj seasons, he would accompany the Prophet to the tribal leaders, praising Islam and calling them to it. In contrast, ʿAlī at that time was too young to be taken seriously, had no wealth to spend, and was not followed. The passage then highlights Abū Bakr's pre-Islamic reputation as a man of opinion, management, and great status, which made the nobles of Quraysh follow him and embrace Islam through his efforts. He endured all kinds of hardships—severities, difficulties, troubles—without his resolve weakening or his firmness softening, without weariness or regret despite the abundance of harm. Instead, he increased daily in support of the religion, strengthening the Prophet and manifesting the symbols of Islam. He vigorously defended the Prophet and the vulnerable believers who had no clan or support. The passage concludes by noting that none of these hardships touched ʿAlī due to his young age, as the enemies did not fear that Islam would spread through his efforts. The final phrase 'and his obvious past merits' ties back to the overall argument for Abū Bakr's precedence.

Key Terms
بذل المال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Abu Bakr say when asked what he left for his children after giving all his wealth?
A) 'I left them nothing.'
B) 'Allah.'
C) 'I left them the religion.'
D) 'I left them my property.'

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's financial sacrifices exemplify complete trust in Allah and selflessness for Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to love the Prophet ﷺ, but when was the last time you spent a significant portion of your wealth for his cause? What holds you back?
?
Abu Bakr left nothing for his children but Allah. What is the greatest material thing you fear losing? How does your trust in Allah compare?
?
When you see Muslims suffering due to their faith, are you willing to use your wealth and even risk your life to help them? What would you sacrifice today?

Abu Bakr's Da'wah and Pre-Islamic Prestige
Describes Abu Bakr's da'wah during Hajj and his pre-Islamic influence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Abu Bakr's role in calling people to Islam during Hajj and his respected status in pre-Islamic times.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr used his pre-Islamic prestige to invite tribal leaders to Islam.

This lesson covers Abu Bakr's efforts during the Hajj seasons, where he accompanied the Prophet to the nobles of the tribes. It also highlights his esteemed position in the Jahiliyyah period, which he used for the benefit of Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read about Abu Bakr's Hajj activities
Read the Arabic passage describing how he went with the Prophet to tribal leaders during Hajj.
2
Note the contrast with Ali
Notice the author's comparison with Ali, who was young and not taken seriously.
This highlights Abu Bakr's unique role.
3
Understand Abu Bakr's pre-Islamic status
Reflect on his reputation as a man of opinion and management, which led many Qurayshi nobles to follow him into Islam.
His status was a vehicle for da'wah.

ثم إنه في جميع المدة التي أقام رسول الله عليه السلام بمكة بعد المبعث إلى وقت الهجرة وهي ثلاث عشرة سنة كان يعاون النبي عليه السلام بماله حتى قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: 'ما نفعني مال ما نفعني مال أبي بكر' حتى ذكر أنه استعان ببعض ماله فبذل جميع ما كان يملكه فقيل : ما تركت لأولادك قال : الله، ونجى الله بماله المعذبين من أيدي الأعداء وبنفسه، وكان في أيام المواسم يطوف مع النبي عليه السلام على من حج من أشراف القبائل، وكان يذكر محاسن الإسلام بين أيديهم، ويرغبهم في الإسلام ويدعوهم إليه، وعلي الله إذ ذاك صغير لا يؤبه لقوله ولا يقتدى به ولا مال ينفق في نصرة الدين، ثم كان أبو بكر في الجاهلية من أهل الرأي والتدبير كبير الشأن، ولعظم مرتبته في ذلك تبعه من ذكرنا من أكابر الناس وعظماء قريش فأسلموا ببركة سعيه ثم إنه تحمل مدة مقامهم بمكة ما تحمل من أنواع المشاق والشدائد و دروب المكاره والمتاعب، فما فترت في تقوية الدين عزيمته ولا لانت عريكته، ولا اعتراه في أثناء ذلك مع طول مقاساته الشدائد سآمة، ولا أدركته على كثرة الأذى من طبقات العدى ندامة بل ازداد في نصرة الدين كل يوم، وتقوية الرسول وإظهار شعار الملة الحنيفية مضاء في الذب عن رسول رب العزة ومن آمن به واتبعه ممن لا عشيرة له فيستظهر بها ولا رهط يعتصم به كفاية وغناء، ولم يكن يمس من تلك الشدائد عليا الله شيء لصغر سنه ووقوع الأمن للأعداء من أن يكون بسعيه للدين انتشار، ويحصل بدعوته للملة أعوان وأنصار، ولسوابقه البادية
Then indeed, during the entire period that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, stayed in Mecca after the mission until the time of emigration, which was thirteen years, he (Abū Bakr) would assist the Prophet, peace be upon him, with his wealth, until he (the Prophet) said, peace and blessings be upon him: 'No wealth has benefited me as the wealth of Abū Bakr has benefited me.' Until it is mentioned that he sought help from some of his wealth, so he gave all that he owned. So it was said: 'What did you leave for your children?' He said: 'Allah.' And Allah saved with his wealth those who were being tortured from the hands of enemies, and with his own person. And during the seasons (of Hajj) he would go around with the Prophet, peace be upon him, to those who had performed Hajj from the nobles of the tribes, and he would mention the beauties of Islam before them, and would encourage them to Islam and call them to it. And ʿAlī, may Allah be pleased with him, at that time was young, his words were not regarded, nor was he followed, nor did he have wealth to spend in support of the religion. Then Abū Bakr in the pre-Islamic period was among the people of opinion and management, great in status, and due to the greatness of his rank in that, those we mentioned among the great people and nobles of Quraysh followed him, so they embraced Islam by the blessing of his effort. Then he bore during their stay in Mecca all kinds of hardships, severities, difficulties, and troubles. His resolve did not slacken in strengthening the religion, nor did his firmness soften, nor did he become weary during that despite the length of enduring hardships, nor did he feel regret despite the abundance of harm from the classes of enemies; rather, he increased every day in supporting the religion, strengthening the Messenger, and manifesting the symbols of the Ḥanīfī faith. He was determined in defending the Messenger of the Lord of Might and those who believed in him and followed him, from those who had no clan to rely on or company to cling to, with sufficiency and wealth. And none of those hardships touched ʿAlī, may Allah be pleased with him, due to his young age and the safety that the enemies felt from his efforts for the religion spreading and his call gaining supporters and helpers. And (by) his obvious past merits...
Source pages p. 1189

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of Abū Bakr's unparalleled sacrifices and steadfastness in supporting Islam during the Meccan period. It begins by emphasizing that throughout the entire thirteen-year period from the Prophet's mission to the Hijra, Abū Bakr assisted the Prophet with his wealth, to the extent that the Prophet declared that no wealth benefited him as much as Abū Bakr's. He then gave all his wealth, and when asked what he left for his children, he simply replied 'Allah,' indicating complete trust in God. Moreover, he used his wealth to free those being tortured by the polytheists, and also risked his own life. During the Hajj seasons, he would accompany the Prophet to the tribal leaders, praising Islam and calling them to it. In contrast, ʿAlī at that time was too young to be taken seriously, had no wealth to spend, and was not followed. The passage then highlights Abū Bakr's pre-Islamic reputation as a man of opinion, management, and great status, which made the nobles of Quraysh follow him and embrace Islam through his efforts. He endured all kinds of hardships—severities, difficulties, troubles—without his resolve weakening or his firmness softening, without weariness or regret despite the abundance of harm. Instead, he increased daily in support of the religion, strengthening the Prophet and manifesting the symbols of Islam. He vigorously defended the Prophet and the vulnerable believers who had no clan or support. The passage concludes by noting that none of these hardships touched ʿAlī due to his young age, as the enemies did not fear that Islam would spread through his efforts. The final phrase 'and his obvious past merits' ties back to the overall argument for Abū Bakr's precedence.

Key Terms
أهل الرأي والتدبير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was Abu Bakr's reputation in the pre-Islamic period according to the passage?
A) A poet
B) A man of opinion and management
C) A warrior
D) A merchant

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr leveraged his pre-Islamic prestige to lead many Qurayshi nobles to Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you use your existing social standing, career influence, or personal reputation to invite others to Islam, or do you let fear of losing status hold you back from following Abu Bakr's example? What one step can you take this week to leverage your position for da'wah?
?
Abu Bakr actively sought out tribal leaders during Hajj to present the beauties of Islam. What are the specific 'beauties of Islam' you can articulate from your own experience, and to whom are you intentionally presenting them?
?
If your current level of influence—whether in your family, workplace, or community—were all you had to call people to Islam, would you be satisfied with your efforts? What would you change starting today?

Abu Bakr's Steadfastness Despite Hardships
Narrates Abu Bakr's endurance of hardships and his continuous strengthening of Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Abu Bakr's unwavering resolve in the face of severe hardships during the Meccan period.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's resolve never slackened despite prolonged hardships.

This lesson details the immense hardships Abu Bakr endured in Mecca and his constant increase in support for Islam. It also includes a comparison with 'Ali, who due to his youth was spared such trials.

Guided Path
1
Read about the hardships
Read the Arabic passage describing the types of hardships Abu Bakr bore.
Look for words like 'مشاق', 'شدائد', 'مكاره', 'متاعب'.
2
Identify the negative states he avoided
Notice that his resolve did not slacken, his firmness did not soften, he did not become weary, and he felt no regret.
These are four qualities he maintained.
3
Observe his daily increase in support
Despite everything, he increased daily in supporting the religion and defending the Prophet.
4
Understand the contrast with Ali
Note that none of these hardships touched Ali due to his young age.
This emphasizes Abu Bakr's unique burden.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ali endured equal or greater hardships in Mecca.
Correction: This passage states that none of those hardships touched Ali due to his young age, while Abu Bakr bore them all.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following did Abu Bakr NOT experience despite the hardships?
A) Slackening of resolve
B) Increase in support for the religion
C) Defending the Prophet
D) Bearing hardships

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's steadfastness in the face of hardships was unmatched; he only increased in support.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face trials for your deen, do you increase in supporting the religion as Abu Bakr did, or do you retreat? What specific step will you take today to emulate his resolve?
?
Abu Bakr felt no regret despite severe harm. Is there a past test where you regretted standing up for the truth? How can you train your heart to reach his level of certainty?
?
Your youth or circumstances may make you think your efforts are inconsequential. But the enemies' perception of Ali's efforts meant he faced fewer hardships. Are you using such excuses to limit your contribution? What will you do this week to strengthen the Messenger's sunnah in your environment?

Abu Bakr's Financial Support and the Prophet's Praise
Narration of Abu Bakr's financial support and prophetic testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the unique significance of Abu Bakr's financial support as acknowledged by the Prophet, including the famous hadith and the story of him giving away all his wealth.

Core Idea
The Prophet declared that no wealth benefited him like Abu Bakr's wealth.

This passage opens a window into Abu Bakr's extraordinary role in early Islam. It begins by noting that many people embraced Islam after coming to the Prophet, then immediately focuses on how Abu Bakr supported the mission with his wealth throughout the thirteen years in Mecca. The centerpiece is a powerful prophetic acknowledgment that sets Abu Bakr apart from all other companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Abu Bakr's wealth
Read the Arabic text and its translation carefully. Notice the flow: first, people accepting Islam, then Abu Bakr's continuous financial support, the Prophet's statement, and finally the account of Abu Bakr giving away all his wealth.
The hadith is a direct quote from the Prophet.
2
Understand the hadith's meaning
Reflect on why the Prophet said 'No wealth has benefited me as the wealth of Abu Bakr has benefited me.' This indicates that Abu Bakr's wealth was uniquely beneficial in the early struggle of Islam.
3
Learn about Abu Bakr's complete sacrifice
When asked what he left for his children, Abu Bakr replied 'Allah'. This shows his absolute trust in God and his priority of supporting the Prophet over personal wealth.

إلى رسول الله عليه السلام فأسلموا ثم إنه في جميع المدة التي أقام رسول الله عليه السلام بمكة بعد المبعث إلى وقت الهجرة وهي ثلاث عشرة سنة كان يعاون النبي عليه السلام بماله حتى قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: "ما نفعني مال ما نفعني مالُ أبي بكر" حتى ذكر أنه استعان ببعض ماله فبذل جميع ما كان يملكه فقيل: ما تركت لأولادك قال: الله، ونجى الله بماله المعذبين من أيدي الأعداء وبنفسه، وكان في أيام المواسم يطوف مع النبي عليه السلام على من حج من أشراف القبائل، وكان يذكر محاسن الإسلام بين أيديهم، ويرغبهم في الإسلام ويدعوهم إليه، وعليٌّ إذ ذاك صغير لا يؤبه لقوله ولا يقتدى به ولا مال ينفق في نصرة الدين، ثم كان أبو بكر في الجاهلية من أهل الرأي والتدبير كبير الشأن، ولعظم مرتبته في ذلك تبعه من ذكرنا من أكابر الناس وعظماء قريش فأسلموا ببركة سعيه ثم إنه تحمل مدة مقامهم بمكة ما تحمل من أنواع المشاق والشدائد ودروب المكاره والمتاعب، فما فترت في تقوية الدين عزيمته ولا لانت عريكته، ولا اعتراه في أثناء ذلك مع طول مقاساته الشدائد سآمة، ولا أدركته على كثرة الأذى من طبقات العدى ندامة بل ازداد في نصرة الدين كل يوم، وتقوية الرسول وإظهار شعار الملة الحنيفية مضاء في الذب عن رسول رب العزة ومن آمن به واتبعه ممن لا عشيرة له فيستظهر بها ولا رهط يعتصم به كفاية وغناء، ولم يكن يمس من تلك الشدائد عليا شيء لصغر سنه ووقوع الأمن للأعداء من أن يكون بسعيه للدين انتشار، ويحصل بدعوته للملة أعوان وأنصار، ولسوابقه البادية غررها وحجولها ومقاماته الشريفة التي [تبخر؟] في ميادين [النفار؟] على ما لغيره من المآثر والمفاخر [تتعقبه؟] رسومها وإغارة نجومها وذيولها
to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and they accepted Islam. Then he, during all the period that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, stayed in Mecca after the mission until the time of the emigration, which was thirteen years, used to aid the Prophet, peace be upon him, with his wealth, until he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'No wealth has benefited me as the wealth of Abu Bakr has benefited me.' Until he mentioned that he sought help from some of his wealth, so he gave all that he owned. It was said: 'What did you leave for your children?' He said: 'Allah.' And Allah saved by his wealth those who were tormented from the hands of enemies, and by himself. And he used to, during the seasons, go around with the Prophet, peace be upon him, to those who performed Hajj from the nobles of the tribes, and he used to mention the good qualities of Islam before them, and encourage them to Islam and call them to it. And Ali at that time was young, his word was not heeded, nor was he followed, nor did he have wealth to spend in supporting the religion. Then Abu Bakr in the pre-Islamic period was among the people of opinion and management, great in status. And due to the greatness of his rank in that, those whom we mentioned from the great people and nobles of Quraysh followed him, and they accepted Islam by the blessing of his effort. Then he bore during their stay in Mecca what he bore of types of hardships and difficulties and paths of unpleasantness and troubles. His determination did not slacken in strengthening the religion, nor did his nature soften. Neither weariness overcame him in that despite his long endurance of hardships, nor did regret befall him despite the abundance of harm from the classes of enemies. Rather, he increased in supporting the religion every day, and in strengthening the Messenger and manifesting the emblem of the Hanifan millah, executing in defending the Messenger of the Lord of Might and those who believed in him and followed him, from those who have no clan by which they could seek support, nor a group to which they could cling, sufficiency and competence. And nothing of those hardships touched Ali due to his young age and the enemies' feeling of security from his effort for the religion spreading and his call to the millah obtaining supporters and helpers. And for his previous good deeds, their bright marks and white legs and noble stations that [rise?] in fields of [war?] over what others have of merits and glories, their traces and the attack of their stars and their tails follow him.
Source pages p. 1189

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative praising Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him). It begins by stating that people came to the Prophet and accepted Islam, then focuses on Abu Bakr's role. The author highlights that throughout the entire thirteen-year Meccan period, Abu Bakr supported the Prophet with his wealth, as confirmed by the hadith 'No wealth has benefited me as the wealth of Abu Bakr has benefited me.' The author then mentions that Abu Bakr gave away all his wealth when asked, and that through his wealth Allah saved persecuted Muslims. Next, the passage describes Abu Bakr's activities during the pilgrimage seasons: he accompanied the Prophet to the tents of tribal leaders, praising Islam and inviting them. In contrast, Ali was young and had no influence or wealth. The author then notes Abu Bakr's high status in pre-Islamic times as a man of opinion and management, and that many Quraysh nobles followed him and accepted Islam by his effort. The passage then describes Abu Bakr's steadfastness during the hardships in Mecca: his determination never slackened, his nature never softened, he felt no weariness or regret, and he only increased in supporting the religion and defending the Prophet and the believers, especially those without clan support. The author contrasts this with Ali, who was untouched by those hardships because he was young and the enemies did not fear his influence. The passage concludes with a reference to Abu Bakr's previous good deeds, likening them to bright marks and noble stations that [rise] in fields of [war] over others' merits, with their traces and attack following him.

أبو بكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say about Abu Bakr's wealth?
A) 'Abu Bakr's wealth is the best wealth.'
B) 'No wealth has benefited me as the wealth of Abu Bakr has benefited me.'
C) 'Abu Bakr's wealth is for Allah.'
D) 'The wealth of Abu Bakr is like none other.'

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's unique praise of Abu Bakr's wealth establishes Abu Bakr's unparalleled financial sacrifice for Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet were to evaluate your wealth today, could he say it benefits him as much as Abu Bakr's? What specific changes would you need to make for your resources to serve Allah's cause that way?
?
Abu Bakr gave everything and said 'Allah' when asked what he left for his children. Is there any possession or relationship you are clinging to because you don't truly believe Allah will provide? What is one step you can take today to release that grip?
?
The Prophet singled out Abu Bakr's wealth as uniquely beneficial. Think of your own spending: how much of it is directed toward the mission of Islam versus your own comfort? What would it cost you to reallocate even 10% from the latter to the former? Are you willing to do it?

Abu Bakr's Preaching and Pre-Islamic Status
Description of Abu Bakr's preaching efforts and his pre-Islamic stature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Bakr used his personal prestige and wisdom to preach Islam and attract influential Quraysh to the faith.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's pre-Islamic reputation as a wise leader made him a powerful advocate for Islam.

The passage now shifts from Abu Bakr's financial support to his active preaching efforts. It describes how he accompanied the Prophet during the pilgrimage seasons to invite tribal leaders, and then highlights his high status in pre-Islamic times. This sets the stage for understanding why so many notable Quraysh followed him.

Guided Path
1
Read about Abu Bakr's preaching during seasons
Read the section starting with 'وكان في أيام المواسم'. Note that Abu Bakr would go around with the Prophet to the nobles of the tribes, praising Islam and inviting them.
This shows Abu Bakr was not just a financial supporter but an active da'wa participant.
2
Contrast with Ali's situation
Notice the author's comparison: while Abu Bakr was active, Ali was young, not listened to, and lacked wealth. This highlights the different roles of the early companions.
3
Learn about Abu Bakr's pre-Islamic reputation
The passage states that Abu Bakr was a man of opinion and management in the Jahiliyyah, and many great Quraysh followed him and accepted Islam by his effort. Reflect on how his established authority served Islam.

إلى رسول الله عليه السلام فأسلموا ثم إنه في جميع المدة التي أقام رسول الله عليه السلام بمكة بعد المبعث إلى وقت الهجرة وهي ثلاث عشرة سنة كان يعاون النبي عليه السلام بماله حتى قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: "ما نفعني مال ما نفعني مالُ أبي بكر" حتى ذكر أنه استعان ببعض ماله فبذل جميع ما كان يملكه فقيل: ما تركت لأولادك قال: الله، ونجى الله بماله المعذبين من أيدي الأعداء وبنفسه، وكان في أيام المواسم يطوف مع النبي عليه السلام على من حج من أشراف القبائل، وكان يذكر محاسن الإسلام بين أيديهم، ويرغبهم في الإسلام ويدعوهم إليه، وعليٌّ إذ ذاك صغير لا يؤبه لقوله ولا يقتدى به ولا مال ينفق في نصرة الدين، ثم كان أبو بكر في الجاهلية من أهل الرأي والتدبير كبير الشأن، ولعظم مرتبته في ذلك تبعه من ذكرنا من أكابر الناس وعظماء قريش فأسلموا ببركة سعيه ثم إنه تحمل مدة مقامهم بمكة ما تحمل من أنواع المشاق والشدائد ودروب المكاره والمتاعب، فما فترت في تقوية الدين عزيمته ولا لانت عريكته، ولا اعتراه في أثناء ذلك مع طول مقاساته الشدائد سآمة، ولا أدركته على كثرة الأذى من طبقات العدى ندامة بل ازداد في نصرة الدين كل يوم، وتقوية الرسول وإظهار شعار الملة الحنيفية مضاء في الذب عن رسول رب العزة ومن آمن به واتبعه ممن لا عشيرة له فيستظهر بها ولا رهط يعتصم به كفاية وغناء، ولم يكن يمس من تلك الشدائد عليا شيء لصغر سنه ووقوع الأمن للأعداء من أن يكون بسعيه للدين انتشار، ويحصل بدعوته للملة أعوان وأنصار، ولسوابقه البادية غررها وحجولها ومقاماته الشريفة التي [تبخر؟] في ميادين [النفار؟] على ما لغيره من المآثر والمفاخر [تتعقبه؟] رسومها وإغارة نجومها وذيولها
to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and they accepted Islam. Then he, during all the period that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, stayed in Mecca after the mission until the time of the emigration, which was thirteen years, used to aid the Prophet, peace be upon him, with his wealth, until he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'No wealth has benefited me as the wealth of Abu Bakr has benefited me.' Until he mentioned that he sought help from some of his wealth, so he gave all that he owned. It was said: 'What did you leave for your children?' He said: 'Allah.' And Allah saved by his wealth those who were tormented from the hands of enemies, and by himself. And he used to, during the seasons, go around with the Prophet, peace be upon him, to those who performed Hajj from the nobles of the tribes, and he used to mention the good qualities of Islam before them, and encourage them to Islam and call them to it. And Ali at that time was young, his word was not heeded, nor was he followed, nor did he have wealth to spend in supporting the religion. Then Abu Bakr in the pre-Islamic period was among the people of opinion and management, great in status. And due to the greatness of his rank in that, those whom we mentioned from the great people and nobles of Quraysh followed him, and they accepted Islam by the blessing of his effort. Then he bore during their stay in Mecca what he bore of types of hardships and difficulties and paths of unpleasantness and troubles. His determination did not slacken in strengthening the religion, nor did his nature soften. Neither weariness overcame him in that despite his long endurance of hardships, nor did regret befall him despite the abundance of harm from the classes of enemies. Rather, he increased in supporting the religion every day, and in strengthening the Messenger and manifesting the emblem of the Hanifan millah, executing in defending the Messenger of the Lord of Might and those who believed in him and followed him, from those who have no clan by which they could seek support, nor a group to which they could cling, sufficiency and competence. And nothing of those hardships touched Ali due to his young age and the enemies' feeling of security from his effort for the religion spreading and his call to the millah obtaining supporters and helpers. And for his previous good deeds, their bright marks and white legs and noble stations that [rise?] in fields of [war?] over what others have of merits and glories, their traces and the attack of their stars and their tails follow him.
Source pages p. 1189

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative praising Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him). It begins by stating that people came to the Prophet and accepted Islam, then focuses on Abu Bakr's role. The author highlights that throughout the entire thirteen-year Meccan period, Abu Bakr supported the Prophet with his wealth, as confirmed by the hadith 'No wealth has benefited me as the wealth of Abu Bakr has benefited me.' The author then mentions that Abu Bakr gave away all his wealth when asked, and that through his wealth Allah saved persecuted Muslims. Next, the passage describes Abu Bakr's activities during the pilgrimage seasons: he accompanied the Prophet to the tents of tribal leaders, praising Islam and inviting them. In contrast, Ali was young and had no influence or wealth. The author then notes Abu Bakr's high status in pre-Islamic times as a man of opinion and management, and that many Quraysh nobles followed him and accepted Islam by his effort. The passage then describes Abu Bakr's steadfastness during the hardships in Mecca: his determination never slackened, his nature never softened, he felt no weariness or regret, and he only increased in supporting the religion and defending the Prophet and the believers, especially those without clan support. The author contrasts this with Ali, who was untouched by those hardships because he was young and the enemies did not fear his influence. The passage concludes with a reference to Abu Bakr's previous good deeds, likening them to bright marks and noble stations that [rise] in fields of [war] over others' merits, with their traces and attack following him.

Key Terms
عشيرة
حنيفية
رأي
تدبير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Abu Bakr do during the pilgrimage seasons?
A) He performed Hajj alone.
B) He went around with the Prophet inviting tribal leaders to Islam.
C) He collected money for the poor.
D) He stayed home and prayed.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr used his pre-Islamic stature as a wise leader to effectively invite influential Quraysh to Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Who in your life is looking to you because of your reputation? Are you using your influence—whether social, professional, or within your family—to bring them closer to Islam, or are you wasting it? What concrete step will you take this week to follow Abu Bakr’s example?
?
Abu Bakr’s status was built on wisdom and management (أهل الرأي والتدبير) even before Islam. What pre-Islamic qualities do you possess that could be redirected for da’wah? Have you ever thought about your natural strengths (like being trusted, organized, or persuasive) as tools for Islam? If not, what is holding you back?
?
The passage contrasts Abu Bakr’s effectiveness with Ali’s youth. Are you using your age or stage of life as an excuse not to contribute? Whether young or old, what can you do today to become a person whose words are heeded and whose actions guide others to truth?

Life of Imam al-Nasafi Maturidi

Abu Bakr's Steadfastness and Contrast with Ali
Description of Abu Bakr's steadfastness and contrast with Ali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate Abu Bakr's unwavering steadfastness in the face of hardships and understand how his role differed from that of Ali due to age and circumstances.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's determination only grew stronger with adversity, never faltering despite prolonged hardship.

The final section of this passage paints a vivid picture of Abu Bakr's endurance and resilience. It describes how he endured various hardships during the Meccan period without any slackening of determination or regret. On the contrary, his support for the religion increased daily. The passage also contrasts his experience with that of Ali, who was spared these difficulties due to his youth. A closing metaphor praises Abu Bakr's earlier deeds as brilliant marks behind him.

Guided Path
1
Read about Abu Bakr's steadfastness
Read the Arabic text from 'ثم إنه تحمل' to the end. Notice the series of negations: his determination did not slacken, his nature did not soften, no weariness, no regret. Instead, he only increased in support.
The text uses parallel negative constructions to emphasize his unyielding nature.
2
Analyze the contrast with Ali
The passage states that nothing of those hardships touched Ali because of his young age and the enemies' lack of concern. Reflect on how the early community experienced different levels of trial.
3
Reflect on the closing praise
The author ends with a poetic description of Abu Bakr's previous good deeds, likening them to bright marks and noble stations that surpass others. This figurative language underscores his unparalleled merits.
The words 'غررها وحجولها' are metaphorical: 'غرر' means white marks on foreheads (of horses), a sign of beauty; 'حجول' means white marks on legs.

?

?

?
The enemies felt secure from Ali's efforts because he was young and they thought his call would not spread. Do you underestimate the impact of your own small or quiet acts of faith? What hidden act of support can you perform today that might seem insignificant but could be powerful?

Abu Bakr's Companionship and Role After the Prophet
Description of the Prophet's trust in Abu Bakr and his role in the caliphate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the multiple evidences of Abu Bakr's virtue and his role in the caliphate as presented by Imam al-Nasafi.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's virtue is proven by the Prophet's trust and the companions' consensus.

This passage from Tabsirat al-Adilla by Imam al-Nasafi highlights the immense trust the Prophet placed in Abu Bakr, from the Hijra to the Battle of Badr. It also points to the unity of the companions after the Prophet's death as a key evidence of his precedence. Let's examine the specific proofs mentioned.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the Prophet's trust
Notice how the author lists specific actions: choosing him for Hijra, companionship, and commanding him to assist with his wealth.
2
Identify the two pledges
The passage refers to the pledges of 'Aqaba and under the tree (Bay'at al-Ridwan). Abu Bakr was first and most eager.
3
Reflect on the Prophet's words at Badr
The Prophet declares Abu Bakr as an intimate, companion, and vizier. Consider the significance of this public affirmation.
4
Understand the evidence from consensus
After the Prophet's death, despite fear, the companions united upon Abu Bakr. This is presented as a strong sign of his merit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقعت لرسول الله عليه السلام به الثقة حتى اختصه لهجرته واختاره لصحبته، وأمره بمعونته بما تحويه يده في سفرته، ثم هو الله أولهم في البيعتين وأحرصهم عليهما، ثم إن الله تعالى لَقَدْ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ إِذْ يُبَايِعُونَكَ تَحْتَ الشَّجَرَةِ فكان له فيهما مثل ثواب من وجدنا منه، ثم كان طول عمر النبي عليه السلام عن يمينه في مجلسه، وكان عند النوائب مستشاره، وفي المهمات وزيره حتى كان يوم بدر مع رسول الله عليه السلام في العريش فانصرف أعرابي عن المصاف فقال: اشتجر الحرب بأصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فاخرج يا أبا بكر فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "إن الله جعل أبا بكر لنبيه أنيسا وجليسا ووزيرا" فانصرف الأعرابي يقول: بخ بخ يا ابن أبي قحافة، ثم إنه له كان أعظم الناس في عيون الصحابة وأجلهم في قلوبهم ولهذا قال أبو عبيدة لعمر - رضي الله عنهما حين قال له عمر: ابسط يدك أبايعك -: أتقول هذا وأبو بكر حاضر والله ما لك في الإسلام فَهَةٌ إلا هذا - فرآه أولى الجماعة بالإمامة، ثم لو لم يكن من دلائل فضيلته وتقدمه على كافة الصحابة إلا ما حصل من القلوب ولم الشعت واجتماع الكلمة بعد وفاة رسول الله عليه السلام مع استيلاء الوجل والخوف على الصحابة لكان ذلك دليلاً كافيا، وكذا ذلك من أدل الدلائل تألف
Trust fell upon him from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, until he singled him out for his emigration and chose him for his companionship, and commanded him to assist him with what his hand possessed in his journey. Then he, by Allah, was the first of them in the two pledges and the most eager for them. Then Allah the Exalted said: 'Indeed Allah was pleased with the believers when they pledged allegiance to you under the tree' (Quran 48:18). So he had in them the like of the reward of those whom we found from him. Then he, throughout the lifetime of the Prophet, peace be upon him, was at his right hand in his assembly, and was his consultant in calamities, and his vizier in important matters. Until the day of Badr when he was with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, in the hut. A Bedouin turned away from the battlefield and said: 'The war has become entangled among the companions of the Messenger of Allah, so come out, O Abu Bakr.' Then the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Indeed Allah has made Abu Bakr for His Prophet an intimate, a companion, and a vizier.' So the Bedouin turned away saying: 'Bravo, bravo, O son of Abu Quhafa.' Then he was the greatest of people in the eyes of the companions and the most majestic in their hearts. For this reason, Abu Ubayda said to Umar - may Allah be pleased with them both, when Umar said to him: 'Extend your hand so I may pledge allegiance to you' -: 'Do you say this while Abu Bakr is present? By Allah, you have no [merit?] in Islam except this.' So he saw him as the most deserving of the community for the imamate. Then, if there were no evidence of his virtue and precedence over all the companions except what was attained in hearts and the gathering of the scattered and the unification of the word after the death of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, with the overcoming of fear and dread upon the companions, that would be sufficient evidence. And indeed that is among the strongest evidences.
Source pages p. 1190

Commentary
This passage continues the biographical praise of Abu Bakr. It begins by stating that the Prophet placed his full trust in Abu Bakr, choosing him specifically for the emigration (hijrah) and companionship, and commanding him to use his wealth for the journey. Next, it mentions that Abu Bakr was the first in the two pledges (the pledge of 'Aqaba and the pledge under the tree) and the most eager for them. The author then quotes Quran 48:18 to highlight divine pleasure with those who pledged under the tree, and states that Abu Bakr received the same reward as those from whom he (the Prophet) found benefit. The passage then describes Abu Bakr's constant presence at the Prophet's right side throughout his lifetime, serving as consultant in calamities and vizier in important matters. The author gives a specific example from the Battle of Badr: when a Bedouin reported the battle's intensity, the Prophet affirmed Abu Bakr's role as 'an intimate, a companion, and a vizier,' causing the Bedouin to express praise. The passage then notes that Abu Bakr was the greatest in the eyes and hearts of the companions, evidence of which is the event where Umar proposed Abu Ubayda for the caliphate, but Abu Ubayda refused, saying that Abu Bakr was more deserving. The author concludes that even if there were no other proof of Abu Bakr's virtue and precedence, the fact that after the Prophet's death, amidst fear and dread, the hearts of the companions united upon him and the word was gathered, is sufficient evidence. This clearly indicates his status as the most deserving of the imamate.

Key Terms
هجرة
البيعتان
صحبة
وزير
إمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Abu Bakr's virtue is only from hadith and not from the consensus of the companions.
Correction: The author argues that the consensus of the companions after the Prophet's death, when they united upon Abu Bakr despite fear, is itself a strong evidence of his virtue, independent of specific hadith.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say about Abu Bakr at the Battle of Badr?
A) 'Abu Bakr is my best friend.'
B) 'Indeed Allah has made Abu Bakr for His Prophet an intimate, a companion, and a vizier.'
C) 'Abu Bakr is the first in paradise.'
D) 'Abu Bakr is the most generous.'

Key Takeaway
The passage demonstrates that Abu Bakr's precedence is established through both explicit prophetic statements and the consensus of the companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet entrusted Abu Bakr with his life and wealth. Is there anything in your life you are withholding from Allah out of fear, or do you trust Him with your most precious possessions?
?
When the companions were most fearful after the Prophet's death, they united upon Abu Bakr. In your moments of fear and uncertainty, where do you seek leadership and stability? Is your heart anchored in the Sunnah and the consensus of the Sahabah?
?
The Prophet called Abu Bakr 'intimate, companion, and vizier.' Which of these roles is missing in your relationship with the Prophet? Are you intimate with his teachings, a companion to his Sunnah, or a vizier spreading his message? What will you change today to fill that gap?

Life of Imam al-Nasafi Maturidi
intermediate
8 min
Proofs from the Prophet's Life and Companions' Consensus
Al-Nasafi enumerates proofs of Abu Bakr's virtue from Prophetic life and Companions' consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical and textual proofs that Al-Nasafi presents for Abu Bakr's virtue during the Prophet's lifetime and the early consensus of the Companions.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's unique closeness to the Prophet and the Companions' recognition establish his superiority.

Al-Nasafi begins by recounting events from the Prophet's life that demonstrate Abu Bakr's special status. From the hijra to the Battle of Badr, and culminating in the acknowledgment of the Companions, these proofs form the foundation for his claim to the caliphate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Abu Bakr's hijra and companionship
Read the first part of the passage that describes how the Prophet chose Abu Bakr for the hijra and for companionship. Notice the repeated emphasis on trust and selection.
The hijra is a key moment of intimacy and trust.
2
Identify the Qur'anic reference and the Badr incident
Find the verse about the pledge under the tree (48:18) and the story of the Bedouin at Badr. Note how the Prophet's praise of Abu Bakr is recorded.
The Prophet calls Abu Bakr 'an intimate companion and vizier'.
3
Analyze the statement of Abu Ubayda
Examine the exchange between Abu Ubayda and Umar. Abu Ubayda's statement 'you have no distinction in Islam except this' is a strong proof of consensus among the Companions that Abu Bakr is the most worthy.
This consensus is a central argument for Sunni imamate.
4
Reflect on how these proofs connect to imamate
Consider how each proof contributes to establishing Abu Bakr's precedence. The lesson concludes that the Companions saw him as 'the most worthy of the congregation for the imamate'.

غررها وحجولها ومقاماته الشريفة التي تبخر في ميادين النفار على ما لغيره من المآثر والمفاخر تتعقبه رسومها وإغارة نجومها وذيولها وقعت لرسول الله عليه السلام به الثقة حتى اختصه لهجرته واختاره لصحبته، وأمره بمعونته بما تحويه يده في سفرته، ثم هو الله أولهم في البيعتين وأحرصهم عليهما، ثم إن الله تعالى لَقَدْ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ إِذْ يُبَايِعُونَكَ تَحْتَ الشَّجَرَةِ فكان له فيهما مثل ثواب من وجدنا منه، ثم كان طول عمر النبي عليه السلام عن يمينه في مجلسه، وكان عند النوائب مستشاره، وفي المهمات وزيره حتى كان يوم بدر مع رسول الله عليه السلام في العريش فانصرف أعرابي عن المصاف فقال : اشتجر الحرب بأصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فاخرج يا أبا بكر فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "إن الله جعل أبا بكر لنبيه أنيسا وجليسا ووزيرًا" فانصرف الأعرابي يقول : بخ بخ يا ابن أبي قحافة، ثم إنه له كان أعظم الناس في عيون الصحابة وأجلهم في قلوبهم ولهذا قال أبو عبيدة لعمر - رضي الله عنهما حين قال له عمر: ابسط يدك أبايعك-: أتقول هذا وأبو بكر حاضر والله ما لك في الإسلام فَهَةٌ إلا هذا - فرآه أولى الجماعة بالإمامة، ثم لو لم يكن من دلائل فضيلته وتقدمه على كافة الصحابة إلا ما حصل من القلوب ولم الشعت واجتماع [؟] الكلمة بعد وفاة رسول الله عليه السلام مع استيلاء الوجل والخوف على الصحابة لكان ذلك دليلاً كافيًا، وكذا ذلك من أدل الدلائل على قوة عقله، وإصابة تدبيره، ورباطة جأشه، وغاية شجاعته، وقلة مبالاته بلومة اللائمين، فإن الصحابة - رضي الله عنهم - كانوا لما حزبهم الأمر العظيم والخطب الهائل الجليل بوفاة رسول الله تحيروا في ذلك، حتى كان منهم من أنكر موته كراهة شق عصا المسلمين وتفرق كلمتهم، ومنهم من ادعى حياته عليه السلام لما ظن أنه لا يموت إذ هو خاتم الأنبياء، فهو عند ذلك ثبت قلبه ولم يتحير في أمره، وما ذهل عن رأيه عند نزول الخطب الذي لمثله يكترث ولدى حلوله إِنَّكَ مَيِّتٌ وَإِنَّهُم مَّيِّتُونَ ثم أنفذ جيش أسامة على خوف المسلمين التفرق والانقلاب وقال : لا أحل لواء عقده رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم إنه فعل ما فعل بأهل الردة وبمانعي الزكاة فهدى الله تعالى ببركة سعيه العرب بعدما نكصوا عن الدين على أعقابهم وارتدوا على أدبارهم، والله الموفق. وكذا تفويض النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام أمر الصلاة إليه مع قوله عليه السلام: "يؤمكم أقرؤكم لكتاب الله تعالى" الحديث، دل أنه كان أفضلهم، ولهذا قال له علي لما قال: أقيلوني فقام علي فقال : لا نقيلك ولا نستقيلك قدمك رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا نؤخرك رضيك لديننا فرضيناك لدنيانا وكذا لما قال أبو سفيان لعلي حين بويع أبو بكر : ما بال هذا الأمر فى أذل قبيلة من قريش، لو شئت لملأتها فرسانا ورجالا فقال له علي: اسكت، والله ما هذا برأي أبي سفيان.
Its brilliant points, its beauties, and its noble stations that float in the fields of nobility beyond the achievements and glories of others, their traces and attacks of their stars and tails follow them. They occurred to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, with trust until he singled him out for his emigration and chose him for his companionship, and commanded him to aid him with what his hand contained in his journey. Then he is, by Allah, the first of them in the two pledges and the most eager for them. Then Allah Almighty said: "Indeed Allah was pleased with the believers when they pledged allegiance to you under the tree" (48:18). So he had in both of them the like of the reward of those we found from him. Then throughout the lifetime of the Prophet, peace be upon him, he was at his right in his assembly, and in calamities he was his consultant, and in important matters his vizier, until the day of Badr when he was with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, in the arish. A Bedouin turned away from the battle line and said: "The war has become entangled with the companions of the Messenger of Allah, so come out, O Abu Bakr." The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: "Indeed Allah made Abu Bakr for His Prophet an intimate companion, a sitting companion, and a vizier." The Bedouin turned away saying: "Bravo, bravo, O son of Abu Quhafa." Then he was the greatest of people in the eyes of the Companions and the most majestic in their hearts. For this reason Abu Ubayda said to Umar, may Allah be pleased with both of them, when Umar said to him: "Extend your hand so I may pledge allegiance to you": "Do you say this while Abu Bakr is present? By Allah, you have no [distinction] in Islam except this." He considered him the most worthy of the congregation for the imamate. Then if there were no proofs of his virtue and his precedence over all the Companions except what was achieved from hearts, the gathering of the scattered, and the unification of the word after the death of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, despite the dominance of fear and fright among the Companions, that would be a sufficient proof. Likewise, that is among the strongest proofs of the strength of his intellect, the correctness of his planning, his composure, his utmost courage, and his disregard for the blame of blamers. For the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, when the great matter and the tremendous, majestic calamity of the death of the Messenger of Allah befell them, they were bewildered about that, until some of them denied his death out of dislike for splitting the staff of the Muslims and the division of their word, and some of them claimed his life, peace be upon him, thinking that he would not die since he is the seal of the prophets. Yet he at that time was firm of heart and not bewildered in his affair, and did not become heedless of his opinion at the occurrence of the calamity, the like of which causes concern and at its descent: "Indeed you are mortal and indeed they are mortal" (39:30). Then he dispatched the army of Usama, despite the Muslims' fear of division and reversal, and said: "I will not untie a banner that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, tied." Then he did what he did with the people of apostasy and the preventers of zakat, and Allah guided the Arabs by the blessing of his effort after they had recoiled from the religion on their heels and apostatized on their backs. Allah is the Grantor of success. Likewise, the delegation by the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, of the matter of prayer to him, along with his saying, peace be upon him: "The one who recites the Book of Allah most among you should lead you" – the hadith – indicates that he was the best of them. For this reason Ali said to him when he said: "Relieve me" – Ali stood up and said: "We will not relieve you nor ask you to be relieved. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, put you forward; we will not put you back. He was pleased with you for our religion, so we are pleased with you for our worldly affairs." Likewise, when Abu Sufyan said to Ali when Abu Bakr was given allegiance: "What is the matter with this matter being in the most contemptible tribe of Quraysh? If you wish, I would fill it with horsemen and men." Ali said to him: "Be quiet, by Allah, this is not the opinion of Abu Sufyan."
Source pages p. 1190

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of historical and textual proofs for the virtue of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, used to establish his superiority over all other Companions and thus his rightful claim to the caliphate. The author, al-Nasafi, presents a series of arguments in narrative form, starting with Abu Bakr's unique closeness to the Prophet during the emigration (hijra) and his being chosen as a companion. He then cites the Qur'anic verse about the pledge under the tree (48:18) to show that Abu Bakr participated and earned reward like all believers. Next, he describes Abu Bakr's constant presence at the Prophet's right hand, his role as advisor and vizier, and a specific incident at the Battle of Badr when the Prophet praised him as an intimate companion and vizier. The author then notes that the Companions themselves considered Abu Bakr the greatest and most majestic, as exemplified by Abu Ubayda's statement to Umar during the Saqifa, where Umar was told that he had no distinction in Islam compared to Abu Bakr. Al-Nasafi then makes a key argument: even if the only proof of Abu Bakr's virtue were the fact that after the Prophet's death, when the Companions were terrified and divided, Abu Bakr managed to unite their hearts and bring them together, that alone would be sufficient proof of his excellence. He then elaborates on this by describing the Companions' bewilderment at the Prophet's death, with some denying it and others claiming he was alive. In contrast, Abu Bakr remained firm, recited the verse 'Indeed you are mortal and indeed they are mortal' (39:30), and took decisive action. He sent the army of Usama despite the risk of division, stating he would not untie a banner tied by the Prophet. He also fought the apostates and those who withheld zakat, and by his efforts, the Arabs were guided back to Islam. Finally, al-Nasafi presents additional proofs: the Prophet's delegation of leading prayer to Abu Bakr, which, according to the hadith about the most qualified to lead prayer, indicates he was the most knowledgeable or best among them. He also cites Ali's statement when he was asked to take the caliphate, in which Ali affirmed Abu Bakr's precedence, and Ali's rebuke of Abu Sufyan when the latter questioned Abu Bakr's tribal status. The overall argument is that Abu Bakr's consistent virtue, leadership, and the consensus of the Companions establish his imamate.

هجرته
صحبته
بيعة الرضوان

عمر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think these proofs are merely historical anecdotes with no theological weight.
Correction: Al-Nasafi presents them as deliberate evidences for Abu Bakr's superiority and rightful imamate, a key Sunni doctrine.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Nasafi, what did the Bedouin hear the Prophet say about Abu Bakr at Badr?
A) 'Abu Bakr is the best of you'
B) 'Indeed Allah made Abu Bakr for His Prophet an intimate companion, a sitting companion, and a vizier'
C) 'Abu Bakr will lead you after me'
D) 'No one can replace Abu Bakr'

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's virtue is established through his unique relationship with the Prophet and the consensus of the Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Abu Bakr's unique closeness to the Prophet is a proof of his virtue, or do you secretly allow doubts about his caliphate to linger in your heart? Examine your inner convictions and repent if needed.
?
When you hear the story of Abu Ubayda rebuking Umar, do you feel the weight of the Companions' consensus? Their agreement was not mere opinion; it was divine guidance. How does this challenge your own judgments about leadership in your community?
?
If you were a Companion at the time, would you have recognized Abu Bakr's superiority as clearly as Abu Ubayda did? What does your answer reveal about your own attachment to status and worldly measures of greatness?

Life of Imam al-Nasafi Maturidi
intermediate
7 min
Proof from Actions After the Prophet's Death
Al-Nasafi presents Abu Bakr's post-Prophet leadership as a proof of his virtue and imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses Abu Bakr's leadership during the crisis after the Prophet's death as a proof for his virtue and imamate.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's firmness and decisive actions after the Prophet's death demonstrate his superior intellect and courage.

Al-Nasafi now argues that even if no other proofs existed, Abu Bakr's ability to unite the Companions after the Prophet's death is itself a sufficient proof of his virtue. He then elaborates on Abu Bakr's composure, his decision to send Usama's army, and his campaign against apostates.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the crisis after the Prophet's death
Read the second part of the passage that describes the Companions' bewilderment and Abu Bakr's firm response. Notice how Al-Nasafi contrasts their confusion with his steadiness.
The Companions were terrified and divided.
2
Identify the key actions: sending Usama's army and fighting apostates
Find where Al-Nasafi mentions Abu Bakr's insistence on sending the army of Usama despite fears, and his war against apostates and zakat-withholders.
These actions required great courage and wisdom.
3
Understand the argument that this alone is sufficient proof
Al-Nasafi states that even if there were no other proofs, this achievement of gathering hearts and uniting the community would be enough. Reflect on why he considers this so significant.
This highlights the theologians' emphasis on practical leadership as a sign of divine favor.
4
Connect to the theme of imamate
Consider how this proof supports Abu Bakr's claim to leadership. The ability to lead in crisis is a clear indication of worthiness.

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of historical and textual proofs for the virtue of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, used to establish his superiority over all other Companions and thus his rightful claim to the caliphate. The author, al-Nasafi, presents a series of arguments in narrative form, starting with Abu Bakr's unique closeness to the Prophet during the emigration (hijra) and his being chosen as a companion. He then cites the Qur'anic verse about the pledge under the tree (48:18) to show that Abu Bakr participated and earned reward like all believers. Next, he describes Abu Bakr's constant presence at the Prophet's right hand, his role as advisor and vizier, and a specific incident at the Battle of Badr when the Prophet praised him as an intimate companion and vizier. The author then notes that the Companions themselves considered Abu Bakr the greatest and most majestic, as exemplified by Abu Ubayda's statement to Umar during the Saqifa, where Umar was told that he had no distinction in Islam compared to Abu Bakr. Al-Nasafi then makes a key argument: even if the only proof of Abu Bakr's virtue were the fact that after the Prophet's death, when the Companions were terrified and divided, Abu Bakr managed to unite their hearts and bring them together, that alone would be sufficient proof of his excellence. He then elaborates on this by describing the Companions' bewilderment at the Prophet's death, with some denying it and others claiming he was alive. In contrast, Abu Bakr remained firm, recited the verse 'Indeed you are mortal and indeed they are mortal' (39:30), and took decisive action. He sent the army of Usama despite the risk of division, stating he would not untie a banner tied by the Prophet. He also fought the apostates and those who withheld zakat, and by his efforts, the Arabs were guided back to Islam. Finally, al-Nasafi presents additional proofs: the Prophet's delegation of leading prayer to Abu Bakr, which, according to the hadith about the most qualified to lead prayer, indicates he was the most knowledgeable or best among them. He also cites Ali's statement when he was asked to take the caliphate, in which Ali affirmed Abu Bakr's precedence, and Ali's rebuke of Abu Sufyan when the latter questioned Abu Bakr's tribal status. The overall argument is that Abu Bakr's consistent virtue, leadership, and the consensus of the Companions establish his imamate.

A) 'I will lead the army myself'
B) 'I will not untie a banner that the Messenger of Allah tied'
C) 'Let the army wait until the community is stable'
D) 'Usama is too young to lead'

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's firmness and decisive actions after the Prophet's death are presented as a powerful proof of his virtue and rightful imamate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a crisis that threatens the unity of your community, do you become bewildered like the Companions or do you stand firm like Abu Bakr? What specific quality from the passage do you need to develop to lead others through trials?
?
Abu Bakr disregarded the blame of blamers to do what he knew was right. In what area of your life are you holding back because you fear criticism? What decision would you make if you knew Allah would guide the outcome through your effort?
?
The Companions denied the Prophet's death out of love and fear of division. When have you clung to an understandable sentiment instead of accepting a painful reality? How can Abu Bakr's example of reciting the Quran and taking decisive action inspire you to move forward?

Proof from Delegation of Prayer and Companions' Endorsement
Al-Nasafi presents delegation of prayer and Companions' endorsements as final proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses the Prophet's delegation of leading prayer to Abu Bakr and the endorsements of Ali and others as proofs for his superiority.

Core Idea
The Prophet's choice of Abu Bakr to lead prayer and the Companions' refusal to replace him confirm his precedence.

Al-Nasafi presents two additional proofs: first, the Prophet appointed Abu Bakr to lead prayer, which according to a hadith indicates he was the most qualified; second, when Ali was offered the caliphate, he himself endorsed Abu Bakr, and Ali rebuked Abu Sufyan for questioning the choice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on delegation of prayer
Read the part where Al-Nasafi cites the Prophet's delegation of prayer to Abu Bakr and the hadith about leading prayer. Understand the logical inference that the one who leads prayer is the best.
The hadith: 'The one who recites the Book of Allah most among you should lead you.'
2
Examine Ali's statement when asked to take the caliphate
Find where Ali says 'We will not relieve you nor ask you to be relieved. The Messenger of Allah put you forward; we will not put you back.' This shows Ali's recognition of Abu Bakr's precedence.
Ali's endorsement is crucial because he was a leading candidate himself.
3
Analyze the incident with Abu Sufyan
Read Ali's rebuke to Abu Sufyan when he criticized Abu Bakr's tribal status. Ali defends Abu Bakr's appointment as not based on tribal opinion.
This underscores that Abu Bakr's imamate is divinely ordained, not a matter of tribal preference.
4
Synthesize the proofs
Consider how these proofs complement the earlier ones. They show that even those who might have claim to leadership (like Ali) acknowledged Abu Bakr's superiority.

غررها وحجولها ومقاماته الشريفة التي تبخر في ميادين النفار على ما لغيره من المآثر والمفاخر تتعقبه رسومها وإغارة نجومها وذيولها وقعت لرسول الله عليه السلام به الثقة حتى اختصه لهجرته واختاره لصحبته، وأمره بمعونته بما تحويه يده في سفرته، ثم هو الله أولهم في البيعتين وأحرصهم عليهما، ثم إن الله تعالى لَقَدْ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ إِذْ يُبَايِعُونَكَ تَحْتَ الشَّجَرَةِ فكان له فيهما مثل ثواب من وجدنا منه، ثم كان طول عمر النبي عليه السلام عن يمينه في مجلسه، وكان عند النوائب مستشاره، وفي المهمات وزيره حتى كان يوم بدر مع رسول الله عليه السلام في العريش فانصرف أعرابي عن المصاف فقال : اشتجر الحرب بأصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فاخرج يا أبا بكر فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "إن الله جعل أبا بكر لنبيه أنيسا وجليسا ووزيرًا" فانصرف الأعرابي يقول : بخ بخ يا ابن أبي قحافة، ثم إنه له كان أعظم الناس في عيون الصحابة وأجلهم في قلوبهم ولهذا قال أبو عبيدة لعمر - رضي الله عنهما حين قال له عمر: ابسط يدك أبايعك-: أتقول هذا وأبو بكر حاضر والله ما لك في الإسلام فَهَةٌ إلا هذا - فرآه أولى الجماعة بالإمامة، ثم لو لم يكن من دلائل فضيلته وتقدمه على كافة الصحابة إلا ما حصل من القلوب ولم الشعت واجتماع [؟] الكلمة بعد وفاة رسول الله عليه السلام مع استيلاء الوجل والخوف على الصحابة لكان ذلك دليلاً كافيًا، وكذا ذلك من أدل الدلائل على قوة عقله، وإصابة تدبيره، ورباطة جأشه، وغاية شجاعته، وقلة مبالاته بلومة اللائمين، فإن الصحابة - رضي الله عنهم - كانوا لما حزبهم الأمر العظيم والخطب الهائل الجليل بوفاة رسول الله تحيروا في ذلك، حتى كان منهم من أنكر موته كراهة شق عصا المسلمين وتفرق كلمتهم، ومنهم من ادعى حياته عليه السلام لما ظن أنه لا يموت إذ هو خاتم الأنبياء، فهو عند ذلك ثبت قلبه ولم يتحير في أمره، وما ذهل عن رأيه عند نزول الخطب الذي لمثله يكترث ولدى حلوله إِنَّكَ مَيِّتٌ وَإِنَّهُم مَّيِّتُونَ ثم أنفذ جيش أسامة على خوف المسلمين التفرق والانقلاب وقال : لا أحل لواء عقده رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم إنه فعل ما فعل بأهل الردة وبمانعي الزكاة فهدى الله تعالى ببركة سعيه العرب بعدما نكصوا عن الدين على أعقابهم وارتدوا على أدبارهم، والله الموفق. وكذا تفويض النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام أمر الصلاة إليه مع قوله عليه السلام: "يؤمكم أقرؤكم لكتاب الله تعالى" الحديث، دل أنه كان أفضلهم، ولهذا قال له علي لما قال: أقيلوني فقام علي فقال : لا نقيلك ولا نستقيلك قدمك رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا نؤخرك رضيك لديننا فرضيناك لدنيانا وكذا لما قال أبو سفيان لعلي حين بويع أبو بكر : ما بال هذا الأمر فى أذل قبيلة من قريش، لو شئت لملأتها فرسانا ورجالا فقال له علي: اسكت، والله ما هذا برأي أبي سفيان.
Its brilliant points, its beauties, and its noble stations that float in the fields of nobility beyond the achievements and glories of others, their traces and attacks of their stars and tails follow them. They occurred to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, with trust until he singled him out for his emigration and chose him for his companionship, and commanded him to aid him with what his hand contained in his journey. Then he is, by Allah, the first of them in the two pledges and the most eager for them. Then Allah Almighty said: "Indeed Allah was pleased with the believers when they pledged allegiance to you under the tree" (48:18). So he had in both of them the like of the reward of those we found from him. Then throughout the lifetime of the Prophet, peace be upon him, he was at his right in his assembly, and in calamities he was his consultant, and in important matters his vizier, until the day of Badr when he was with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, in the arish. A Bedouin turned away from the battle line and said: "The war has become entangled with the companions of the Messenger of Allah, so come out, O Abu Bakr." The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: "Indeed Allah made Abu Bakr for His Prophet an intimate companion, a sitting companion, and a vizier." The Bedouin turned away saying: "Bravo, bravo, O son of Abu Quhafa." Then he was the greatest of people in the eyes of the Companions and the most majestic in their hearts. For this reason Abu Ubayda said to Umar, may Allah be pleased with both of them, when Umar said to him: "Extend your hand so I may pledge allegiance to you": "Do you say this while Abu Bakr is present? By Allah, you have no [distinction] in Islam except this." He considered him the most worthy of the congregation for the imamate. Then if there were no proofs of his virtue and his precedence over all the Companions except what was achieved from hearts, the gathering of the scattered, and the unification of the word after the death of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, despite the dominance of fear and fright among the Companions, that would be a sufficient proof. Likewise, that is among the strongest proofs of the strength of his intellect, the correctness of his planning, his composure, his utmost courage, and his disregard for the blame of blamers. For the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, when the great matter and the tremendous, majestic calamity of the death of the Messenger of Allah befell them, they were bewildered about that, until some of them denied his death out of dislike for splitting the staff of the Muslims and the division of their word, and some of them claimed his life, peace be upon him, thinking that he would not die since he is the seal of the prophets. Yet he at that time was firm of heart and not bewildered in his affair, and did not become heedless of his opinion at the occurrence of the calamity, the like of which causes concern and at its descent: "Indeed you are mortal and indeed they are mortal" (39:30). Then he dispatched the army of Usama, despite the Muslims' fear of division and reversal, and said: "I will not untie a banner that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, tied." Then he did what he did with the people of apostasy and the preventers of zakat, and Allah guided the Arabs by the blessing of his effort after they had recoiled from the religion on their heels and apostatized on their backs. Allah is the Grantor of success. Likewise, the delegation by the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, of the matter of prayer to him, along with his saying, peace be upon him: "The one who recites the Book of Allah most among you should lead you" – the hadith – indicates that he was the best of them. For this reason Ali said to him when he said: "Relieve me" – Ali stood up and said: "We will not relieve you nor ask you to be relieved. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, put you forward; we will not put you back. He was pleased with you for our religion, so we are pleased with you for our worldly affairs." Likewise, when Abu Sufyan said to Ali when Abu Bakr was given allegiance: "What is the matter with this matter being in the most contemptible tribe of Quraysh? If you wish, I would fill it with horsemen and men." Ali said to him: "Be quiet, by Allah, this is not the opinion of Abu Sufyan."
Source pages p. 1190

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of historical and textual proofs for the virtue of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, used to establish his superiority over all other Companions and thus his rightful claim to the caliphate. The author, al-Nasafi, presents a series of arguments in narrative form, starting with Abu Bakr's unique closeness to the Prophet during the emigration (hijra) and his being chosen as a companion. He then cites the Qur'anic verse about the pledge under the tree (48:18) to show that Abu Bakr participated and earned reward like all believers. Next, he describes Abu Bakr's constant presence at the Prophet's right hand, his role as advisor and vizier, and a specific incident at the Battle of Badr when the Prophet praised him as an intimate companion and vizier. The author then notes that the Companions themselves considered Abu Bakr the greatest and most majestic, as exemplified by Abu Ubayda's statement to Umar during the Saqifa, where Umar was told that he had no distinction in Islam compared to Abu Bakr. Al-Nasafi then makes a key argument: even if the only proof of Abu Bakr's virtue were the fact that after the Prophet's death, when the Companions were terrified and divided, Abu Bakr managed to unite their hearts and bring them together, that alone would be sufficient proof of his excellence. He then elaborates on this by describing the Companions' bewilderment at the Prophet's death, with some denying it and others claiming he was alive. In contrast, Abu Bakr remained firm, recited the verse 'Indeed you are mortal and indeed they are mortal' (39:30), and took decisive action. He sent the army of Usama despite the risk of division, stating he would not untie a banner tied by the Prophet. He also fought the apostates and those who withheld zakat, and by his efforts, the Arabs were guided back to Islam. Finally, al-Nasafi presents additional proofs: the Prophet's delegation of leading prayer to Abu Bakr, which, according to the hadith about the most qualified to lead prayer, indicates he was the most knowledgeable or best among them. He also cites Ali's statement when he was asked to take the caliphate, in which Ali affirmed Abu Bakr's precedence, and Ali's rebuke of Abu Sufyan when the latter questioned Abu Bakr's tribal status. The overall argument is that Abu Bakr's consistent virtue, leadership, and the consensus of the Companions establish his imamate.

يؤمكم أقرؤكم
علي
أبو سفيان

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Ali was coerced into endorsing Abu Bakr, but Al-Nasafi presents it as voluntary and sincere.
Correction: Ali's public statement is recorded as a free endorsement, strengthening the consensus.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's appointment of Abu Bakr to lead prayer and the endorsements from Ali and others confirm his superiority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When the Prophet chose Abu Bakr to lead prayer, did you ever feel a secret resistance to that choice? Do you fully submit to the decisions of those whom Allah has placed over you, even when your own preferences differ? Will you today say from your heart, 'قدمك رسول الله' and accept that choice without reservation?
?
Ali refused the caliphate and endorsed Abu Bakr with conviction. Is there a position, a status, or a leadership role you are holding onto out of pride, even though you know someone else deserves it more? What is one concrete step you can take today to step back and support the right person, even at the cost of your own ego?
?
Abu Sufyan appealed to tribal pride to challenge Abu Bakr's caliphacy. Have you ever allowed worldly biases—family, ethnicity, social status—to influence your judgment about who should lead? When you catch such thoughts, do you rebuke them as sharply as Ali did, or do you entertain them silently? What will you do to purify your heart from every trace of prejudice?
